County Public Property Office Requests Exemption from Mu Tax Late Fees 109

One-Tenth Already Given to the Poor

How Can Another One Percent Be Borne?

Jiang Shijie, the director of the Shanghai County Public Property Management Office, and Kang Yongnian, the deputy director, telegraphed Minister Song of the Ministry of Finance and Chairman Gu of the Provincial Government yesterday, stating: "The Shanghai County was instructed by your government to add a 1% late fee to the various mu taxes in accordance with the decision of the 541st committee meeting to be used as education funds. The county was ordered to comply, starting with the second term of land value tax in the 21st year, with a limited time to collect the tax and late fee. The people of the county, upon hearing this, deeply doubted the decision. Tax payment is the obligation of citizens, and education funds already have surcharges. Provincial and county surtaxes are charged a 10% late fee for late payment, which is intended to penalize delayed payment. However, the local surtax mu tax is collected along with the regular tax, and there was no late fee originally. Now, suddenly, there is a provincial order to add a 1% late fee to the tax beyond the limited time. This increases the burden on the people and exacerbates their difficulties. The harvest of the county is not as good as in previous years, and the people's strength has been exhausted. Paying taxes on time is already a struggle. How can the wealthy be penalized for delaying payment? It is known that the 10% penalty has been imposed on the poor, and how can another 1% be borne? Moreover, the central government has repeatedly ordered consideration for farmers. We dare to request that, in accordance with this intention, the late fee should no longer be imposed. Shijie and others are close to the people and are well aware of the increasing poverty of the farmers. We cannot remain silent. We hereby telegraph this matter for your consideration and request that you quickly order the Finance Department to instruct Shanghai County to exempt this late fee from implementation, and we will be deeply grateful."

The Fuhai and Haiying Patrol Ships Ran Aground Successively in Dinghai 111

Officers and Soldiers and Weapons All Evacuated

The Administration Bureau Telegraphed to Find Ways to Rescue

The Fuhai and Haiying patrol ships, which are specially responsible for protecting the sea, were dispatched by the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Fisheries Administration Bureau. The ships left Shenjiamen, Dinghai, early yesterday morning to patrol the sea, but soon ran aground in Heyewan and Putuo waters, respectively. After receiving the telegram, the Shanghai Administration Bureau sent personnel to the scene and telegraphed Dinghai to provide assistance nearby. Details are recorded as follows:

Fuhai Aground: Captain Zhang Ziming of the Fuhai patrol ship, with a total of 36 officers, including special officers, first officer, second officer, chief engineer, second engineer, and soldiers, sailed from Shenjiamen, Dinghai, to Daishan for patrol at 5:00 am on the 19th of this month. At about 6:00 am, when sailing to the Heyewan waters, 60 li away from Dinghai, the ship mistakenly sailed off course and ran aground. First Officer Xin Yuren tried to avoid it, but it was too late. The ship tilted northward and hoisted a flag to request assistance. Fortunately, nearby fishermen saw it and sailed to the rescue in sailboats. They transferred all the officers, soldiers, sailors, and weapons of the ship to sailboats and transported them to Shenjiamen. The office of the bureau there reported to the Shanghai Administration Bureau by telegram.

Haiying Aground: Captain Yang Jingming of the Haiying patrol ship, with a total of 32 officers, including first officer, chief engineer, and soldiers, sailed from Shenjiamen at the same time as the Fuhai at 5:00 am on the 19th of this month to Shanghai. At about 7:00 am, when sailing to the waters off Putuo Mountain, 20 li away from Shenjiamen, the ship encountered fog and ran aground. The ship immediately hoisted a flag to request assistance. Nearby fishing boats, alerted, sailed to the rescue. Fortunately, the ship was not seriously damaged. The officers of the ship were transferred to fishing boats and returned to Shenjiamen to report. The office of the bureau there reported the incident to the Shanghai Administration Bureau by telegram.

Separate Telegrams for Rescue: The patrol ships of the Administration Bureau, including Haihong, Haigu, Haifu, Haiying, Qing'an, Biaohai, and the sixth ship, were all ordered to depart to patrol the waters around Dinghai and other places during this fishing season. Director Chen Zhongsheng and Patrol Commissioner Wang Zhiliang of the Administration Bureau, after receiving the telegram from Shenjiamen, telegraphed the various agencies in Dinghai at 4:00 pm to provide assistance. They also requested that the ships of the Sanbei Company provide assistance when passing the grounding locations of the two patrol ships.

Captain Rushes to Scene: Captain Zhang Ziming of the Fuhai ship, who was in Shanghai on official business, rushed to assist in the rescue by taking the regular Dinghai ship yesterday after receiving news of the ship's grounding. It is also heard that the bottom of the ship was broken after grounding, and seawater entered. It has already sunk. The officers, soldiers, and sailors, along with the weapons, were all rescued. However, the Administration Bureau officially denied this and stated that the Fuhai and Haiying patrol ships are currently being rescued and will be out of danger soon. It is unlikely to sink.

Planned Double-Tracking on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway at Two Locations 115

And Addition and Extension of Passing Sidings

Approved by the Ministry of Railways and Soon to Be Implemented

The Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations previously submitted a request to the Ministry of Railways. To facilitate traffic, develop business, reduce travel time, and avoid train delays, they proposed laying double tracks between Shanghai and Nanxiang, and between Nanjing and Taipingmen. At other stations, they proposed adding five passing sidings where necessary. Yesterday, the Ministry of Railways ordered the Railway Administration that the submitted plan is beneficial for traffic and business and should be approved. It instructed them to re-verify and calculate all budget estimates, attach drawings, and submit funding plans to the Ministry for approval. The "New Voice" News Agency's correspondent in Beijing has obtained the original request from the two Railway Administrations, as follows:

Railway Administration's Submission: Request for Approval. It is noted that the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway has frequent passenger trains, and the traffic at each station is extremely congested. The existing single track is insufficient, leading to situations such as at Nanjing Station, where departing trains are delayed waiting for trains arriving from Zhenjiang, and at Hepingmen Station, where already delayed trains are held to wait for connecting trains. Additionally, stations such as Qiaotouzhen Station lack passing sidings, and other stations have short passing sidings, causing trains to be delayed due to waiting for meetings. This is unavoidable. If improvements are not made, the Railway feels that trains spend too much time at stations, which is uneconomical, and passengers feel that travel is too time-consuming or delayed, which is very inconvenient. Previously, this Bureau instructed the engineering, mechanical, and traffic departments to conduct detailed studies to reduce travel time and avoid delays. The general office also repeatedly ordered thorough improvements. Now, according to the results of the Engineering Department Director's research, it is proposed to lay double tracks between Shanghai and Nanxiang, and between Nanjing and Taipingmen. In other sections, add five passing sidings where necessary, and extend existing passing sidings at each station to 732 meters. A budget of expenses, track materials, and spare parts has been drawn up and checked. The proposed sections are necessary. The original documents are copied and submitted for review. If approved, funding will be arranged to benefit business and convenience passengers. Whether appropriate or not, please instruct to comply. Respectfully submitted (attached copies).

Proposed Plan (Copy): Respectfully submitted, the issue of laying double tracks between Shanghai and Suzhou, adding passing sidings, and extending existing passing sidings has been studied according to instructions. Based on careful research, it is felt that there is no need to lay double tracks between Shanghai and Suzhou. It is believed that the following measures will increase business and alleviate traffic difficulties: (1) Lay double tracks between Shanghai and Nanxiang; (2) Lay double tracks between Nanjing and Taipingmen; (3) Add a passing siding at the 57.5 km mark between Kunshan and Zhengyi, as this area is a large agricultural region and the railway could generate significant revenue; (4) Construct a passing siding at the 92.17 km mark, which is crucial because the distance between Suzhou and Hushu Pass is 12.5 km, and trains are often held at Hushu Pass; (5) Construct a passing siding at the 227 km mark, as the distance between Xinfeng and Zazhe stations is 12.70 km; (6) Construct a passing siding at the 248 km mark between Zhenjiang and Gaozi, as the distance between the two stations is 123.4 km, which will avoid congestion; (7) Construct a 732-meter-long passing siding at Qiaotouzhen Station; (8) Extend the existing 396-meter passing siding at Longtan Station to 732 meters; (9) Other passing sidings should be extended to 732 meters. If double tracks are laid between Shanghai and Nanxiang, and the above-mentioned addition and extension of passing sidings are completed, the current traffic difficulties will be resolved without incurring significant expenses to lay double tracks from Nanxiang to Suzhou, as there is no need to lay double tracks between Nanxiang and Suzhou. Furthermore, it is currently planned to relocate Shanghai North Station to Zhongshan Road and relocate the maintenance depot to the 14 km mark. Therefore, double tracks must be laid between North Station and the depot, and extending these double tracks from the depot to Nanxiang is easy. This is a sufficient reason to lay double tracks between North Station and Nanxiang. Laying double tracks between Nanjing and Taipingmen is extremely important. Currently, Nanjing Station often delays departing trains while waiting for trains arriving from Zhenjiang, and Hepingmen Station often holds already delayed trains to wait for connecting trains. Laying these double tracks will eliminate these problems. For example, on January 31st of this year, Train No. 11 was held at Hepingmen Station for 15 minutes to wait for Train No. 6. If there were double tracks between Nanjing and Taipingmen, Hepingmen Station would not need to hold it. This is just one example. In the future, with the construction of the Nanjing ferry, transportation will become frequent, and such occurrences will become even more common. This is why laying double tracks in this section is crucial. Laying double tracks between Shanghai and Nanxiang will also greatly facilitate the departure of trains from Shanghai. Currently, southbound trains are often held between Nanxiang and Shanghai to wait for northbound trains. This improvement will eliminate this problem.

Mu Ouchu Questions Aviation Salvation Award 116

Writes to Wang Xiaolai for Discussion

Mu Ouchu's letter to Wang Xiaolai regarding the Aviation Salvation Award reads: Elder Brother Xiaolai, greetings. I recently read in the newspaper that the Aviation Salvation Award Committee office has been established, and you and six others have been appointed as standing committee members. Initially, I thought this was initiated by the patriotic enthusiasm of the people, but after reading carefully, I realized that the initiator is a Westerner. I don't know what kind of person this Westerner is, but I heard that he started by selling military arms. Regardless of his motives, if he can donate generously, it would be enough to encourage those of our countrymen who are reluctant to part with their wealth. However, there are problematic statements in the preamble. Initially, it says, "Willing to donate the sale price of his houses and land worth 1.5 million, as well as his collection of antiques, to purchase airplanes and military supplies." Later, it says, "After returning the original price and all expenses." If he is willing to donate everything, then why return the original price? There is a clear contradiction, which raises suspicion. However, this might be a typographical error. But considering item five of the later measures, which states, "Willing to recover half of the value, 750,000 yuan, at the lowest possible estimate," then the preamble's statement about donating everything to purchase airplanes is clearly a form of deception and is quite strange. The land on Daxi Road, measuring 8 mu, 4 fen, 7 li, and 1 hao, what is its value? A four-story Western-style house, what is its value? Unless impartially estimated, there are doubts. As for the land measuring 2 mu, 4 fen, and 1 li, its location is unknown, and its price is even more difficult to estimate. The value of the collection of antiques is even more doubtful. I believe there are three incomprehensible points: First, the award tickets are a disguised form of lottery, which is very harmful to the common people and has been explicitly prohibited by the government. Even if the government issues award tickets to promote the construction of aviation and highways, it is only a temporary expedient measure. If an ordinary Westerner issues award tickets in the name of patriotism to obtain a good price because the market is poor and land, houses, and antiques are difficult to sell, if this trend starts, how will we deal with those who follow suit? This is the first incomprehensible point. Second, celebrities are originally role models for society, and their actions can influence society. Now, they are promoting the sale of a Westerner's land, houses, and antiques with great fanfare, using the weaknesses of the people to issue award tickets. Doing this for others seems to harm the reputation of celebrities. This is the second incomprehensible point. Third, assuming that the land, houses, and antiques are worth 750,000 yuan, at this time of national poverty, 750,000 yuan enters the Westerner's hands under the guise of returning the original price. The remaining 250,000 yuan, purportedly donated to purchase airplanes and military supplies, will inevitably flow into the hands of foreigners. It is a very good plan for the Westerner to easily obtain cash for real estate and antiques. But for our countrymen, it requires spending 1.2 million yuan to purchase non-productive real estate and antiques. This is the third incomprehensible point. Because I have doubts about the above, and because we are friends, I dare to speak frankly and present them to you. I ask you to study this matter further to show caution. I am eagerly looking forward to it. Sincerely, Mu Xiangyue, the 20th day of the 5th month of the 22nd year [of the Republic of China].

Northeast Refugee Association Eagerly Awaits Donations 117

The Shanghai United Association of Charitable Organizations for Relief of Northeast Refugees is organized by nine charitable organizations in this city with the longest history of conducting charitable work. Xu Shiying, Wang Zhen, and Xiong Xiling are publicly elected as chairman and vice-chairmen. Mr. Xu and Mr. Wang are stationed at the association daily. Since the outbreak of war in the Northeast and the catastrophic floods in Jilin and Heilongjiang provinces, at a time when it was mid-winter, the association, regardless of the difficulties, found ways to transport food and cotton clothing and sent personnel to Harbin and other places to distribute them. Tens of thousands of Northeast refugees were saved from freezing and starvation. Subsequently, as the war expanded to inside the customs, the association again dispatched standing committee members Qu Wenliu and Feng Yangshan to reside permanently in Tianjin and Peiping to provide assistance nearby. They also established shelters and soup kitchens in Tangshan, Kailuan, and other places to provide relief to refugees, sparing no effort. Their courageous acts of righteousness have always been admired by society. Previously, when the family members of Commander-in-Chief Wang Delin's troops took refuge in Shanghai, the association, in conjunction with relevant organizations, set up a place to receive them and provided work-study education. Recently, troops under Su Bingwen arrived in Shanghai, and the Municipal Public Security Bureau consulted with the association, and they jointly dispatched personnel to receive them. Upon their initial arrival, the Public Security Bureau advanced more than 590 yuan for automobile, hotel, and food expenses, which the association fully reimbursed. It is heard that all subsequent reception expenses will be borne solely by the association. However, as the war continues, the number of refugees is increasing daily. The association's relief funds are limited, and it is difficult to sustain the effort. It is hoped that people from all walks of life will voluntarily donate and, with patriotic enthusiasm, jointly support this righteous cause of saving the people.

Silk Trade Associations Discuss Silk Industry Relief Measures 121

Elect Representatives to Petition in Beijing

The Shanghai Electric Silk Weaving Industry Association and the Silk Industry Association, in view of the fact that domestic silk products are being seized by the Japanese in overseas markets, attribute the cause to the unusually heavy import duties on rayon, reaching up to 80% ad valorem. This increases the cost of silk fabrics, making it difficult to compete in overseas trade. It is noted that in the past, exports of rayon blended silk fabrics amounted to more than 1 million yuan annually. After the imposition of import duties on rayon last year, silk exports decreased to 2 million yuan. Recently, silk exports have further decreased. If this continues, the future of the silk industry will be difficult to sustain. Yesterday, they held a joint meeting with the Silk Industry Association, with more than ten representatives from both industries, to discuss the matter. The meeting agreed that after the levy of import duties on rayon, the cost of fabrics has increased significantly, making it impossible to export silk fabrics to compete with Japanese silk products. Therefore, both industries elected ten representatives to go to Beijing to petition the Party, government, finance, and industry departments. They will request that all import duties on rayon fabrics and rayon blended fabrics exported to Southeast Asia, India, and other places be refunded, with the aim of competing in trade with Japan and resolving the hidden pain of the domestic silk industry.

Ministry of Finance Consults Municipal Government to Explain Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Collection Methods 123

The Ministry of Finance issued a document to the Shanghai Municipal Government to explain the methods for collecting tobacco and alcohol business taxes. The document states: For consultation purposes, it is noted that in the 20th year [of the Republic of China], this Ministry consulted provincial and municipal governments to explain five methods for collecting business taxes. Item three stated, "For those who exclusively operate tobacco and alcohol businesses and have already paid the central government's tobacco and alcohol license fee, provinces shall not collect business tax from them. However, stores that sell other goods and also sell tobacco and alcohol shall still pay business tax." The above stipulation in the proviso refers to shops mainly engaged in other goods and also selling small quantities of tobacco and alcohol, and whose business income is not easily divided, shall still pay business tax. However, it is noted that the business tax collection regulations of various provinces and cities have not clearly defined the exemption or collection of business tax for stores that also sell liquor and distilleries. Business tax collection agencies often collect the tobacco and alcohol business tax from stores that mainly sell tobacco and alcohol but also sell other goods, causing appeals and disputes among merchants. In September of the 20th year, the Yongjia Sauce Industry Association of Zhejiang submitted a report stating that the Ninth District Business Tax Bureau ordered businesses that also operate distilleries and sauce shops and have already paid the license tax for liquor to pay taxes from March to June, requesting that this be promptly ordered to be eliminated. After investigation by this Ministry, it was determined that stores or distilleries mainly engaged in tobacco and alcohol and also engaged in other goods, whose main business part has already paid the central government's tobacco and alcohol license tax, should be exempt from business tax, while other businesses should still pay business tax to show distinction. The Governor of Zhejiang Province was instructed to comply with this and instruct all business tax collection agencies in the province to comply, and to transfer the taxes paid from March to June to be eliminated. The situation in each province and city is the same and should be handled accordingly to avoid confusion and disputes. In addition to distribution, the relevant case is consulted to your provincial and municipal governments, and the Finance Department is instructed to instruct the competent authorities under its jurisdiction to comply with it, to further publicize the alliance, this consultation to the Shanghai Municipal Government.

Notice to Merchant Ships Navigating Waters of the Change of Steering Gear Command 127

Berlade, the Customs Commissioner of the Jianghai Customs, issued a notice yesterday regarding the change of steering gear command for merchant ships navigating the waters, which stated: For the purpose of issuing notices, it is now ordered by the government that all Chinese merchant ship steering gear commands (i.e., driving commands used to convey to the helmsman) shall be implemented with direct meaning from twelve o'clock midnight on May 13th of this year. For example, when the ship is moving forward and the rudder wheel, rudder blade, and bow are to turn to the right, use the English word "Right" to command it. Conversely, if the rudder wheel, rudder blade, and bow are to turn to the left, use the English word "Left" to command it. For ships using manual steering, the commands used must also be handled uniformly, that is, "Right" commands the rudder blade and bow to the right, "Left" commands the rudder blade and bow to the left, etc. Hereby, all shipping merchants are notified accordingly. This is a special announcement.

Mistaking Iodine for Stomach Medicine 133

After Drinking, Consciousness Blurred, Abdominal Pain Like a Knife

Sent to a Relief Center for Treatment, Fortunate to Recover

Qiu Qiaosheng, a 23-year-old from Chuansha, residing at No. 11 Gujia Alley in the Nanshi area, works as a mail sorter, number 723, in the import section of the 18th branch of the post office on Avenue Joffre. Yesterday, being Sunday and therefore a day off, he was resting at home when he suddenly felt dizzy, with a severe onset. His mother-in-law, Zhang Ding, seeing his condition, became very anxious and immediately took a large spoonful of stomach medicine, mixed it with water, and had him drink it. Unexpectedly, not long after drinking it, his consciousness became blurred and his abdominal pain intensified. He was rushed by car to various hospitals in the Nanshi area for treatment, but all were closed on Sunday. He was then taken to the First Relief Hospital of the Chinese Relief Association at the intersection of Rue de Course and Rue Longmen. After examination by the hospital's doctor, his pulse was 140 beats per minute and his temperature was 39 degrees Celsius. Upon testing the stomach medicine he had taken, it was found to be iodine by mistake. After surgery and the administration of an antidote, he was fortunate enough to recover.

丨Started Due to Wage Dispute丨

Silk Factory Owner Abuses Apprentices with Cruel Methods 139

Burning Legs and Arms with Red-Hot Iron Rods

Neighbors Report to the Authorities Out of Dissatisfaction

Zhang Linquan, a 16-year-old apprentice from Jiangyin at the Tongchang Silk Factory on Rue Robert in Shanghai's west, is very honest and hardworking. He had only been studying at the factory for about a year when the January 28th Shanghai Incident broke out, and the factory stopped working. The apprentice, also frightened, returned to his hometown. He had a package of clothes that he left at the factory because it was inconvenient to carry it at the time. Later, in the eighth month of the lunar calendar, Zhang came to Shanghai to work at the factory. He asked the factory owner for his package of clothes, but the factory owner kept evading him. Later, he learned that the clothes had been pawned. Zhang was even more worried and asked for them more urgently. Later, he changed to asking for the pawn ticket, but he was not given it either. Late last month, Zhang sent a letter to his father. On the 12th of this month, the factory owner, Xu Baoyuan, suddenly received a letter from Zhang's father. Xu opened it and read it. Because the wording in the letter contained a slight sense of insult, and since Xu had several friends next to him, he felt that he had been insulted and was very angry. Xu immediately threw the letter aside and left the factory with his friends. Unexpectedly, Xu's younger brother, Xu Caiyuan, and his unmarried brother-in-law, Xue Yinquan, also became angry out of shame. They immediately tied up the apprentice, Zhang Linquan, with a rope. Xu then placed an iron rod in the furnace to heat it red-hot and burned Zhang's arms all over. He also stabbed Zhang's arms and legs, causing Zhang to faint from the pain. Xue then beat him with a stick, causing blood to flow from his arms and legs, a gruesome sight. After a while, the factory owner, Xu Baoyuan, returned to the factory and saw Zhang lying unconscious on the ground with wounds all over his body. Knowing that he had caused trouble, he immediately took Zhang to the hospital for treatment. By the time Zhang's wounds had healed slightly on the 20th, he left the hospital and rushed to his mother's place. His mother, seeing her son suffering such cruelty, asked about what happened and immediately burst into tears, crying loudly. The matter was heard by neighbors, who came to see what was happening and were all indignant. They then swarmed Zhang Linquan to the district office to file a complaint. The district chief ordered the police to arrest the Xu brothers and Xue Yinquan. After questioning by District Officer Jiang, the factory owner, Xu Baoyuan, confessed that he was out at the time and did not know what had happened. After seeing that Zhang had been injured, he immediately took him to the hospital and severely scolded his younger brother, Caiyuan. Xu Caiyuan confessed that the apprentice had teased his younger sister, Rongmei, so he beat him. Xue Yinquan and Xu Rongmei confessed similarly. After obtaining their confessions, District Officer Jiang, believing that the Xus had dared to use such cruel methods to burn and beat the apprentice, causing him to be covered in wounds, was extremely cruel. He sentenced them to detention pending a document to be sent to the local court for further investigation according to law.

Mei Lanfang Will Perform Again 140

Tianchan Invites Supporting Actors

The famous actor Mei Lanfang, after being hired to come south by Tianchan last time and ceasing to perform after the term expired, resided in Cangzhou Villa on Jing'an Temple Road with his family due to the unrest in North China. Ten Yuan Still Not Enough to Satisfy Desire

Liu Aguo, from Changzhou, lives in a bungalow without a number on Songpan Road and makes a living by growing vegetables. He previously became acquainted with a widow in Yinxiang Port and brought her back to live with him to help with the work. This was heard by the Yangzhou hoodlum Lu Meijin. On the morning of the 16th of this month at 10 a.m., he went to Liu to extort 16 yuan for a wedding feast, saying that only then would there be no trouble. Liu, fearing his ferocity, had no choice but to hand over his clothes to him, and Lu took them to a nearby pawnshop, pawned them for 10 yuan, and left. Unexpectedly, the day before yesterday, he and his friend Zhou Yunlong, from Qingjiang, went again to demand 6 yuan, claiming that it was for the cost of the meal at the Hongyun Restaurant at No. 1867 Yangshupu Road and that there was a detailed bill that had to be paid in full, otherwise they would beat him to death. A Large Number of Japanese Blood Flukes Discovered in the Qingyang Port Riverbank 142

丨Dr. Robertson Sends a Letter to the Health Bureau Requesting Attention丨

Dr. Robertson of the Lester Institute of Medical Research in this city sent a letter yesterday to Li Ting'an, Director of the Shanghai Health Bureau, stating that on Sunday, the 14th of this month, he and several technicians from the Institute's Laboratory went to Qingyang Port, near the Yacht Club, to inspect the area. They collected a large number of snails and other similar creatures from the small beaches and riverbanks there. These mollusks are intermediate hosts for Japanese blood flukes. After returning to Shanghai, the Parasitology Department of the Institute's Laboratory examined them and found that these snails were indeed heavily infected. The attached map marks the locations where the infected snails were found with white crosses. This matter should be publicly announced to alert those who camp and swim in the area. It is my responsibility to deliver this announcement. The area near Shiqiao, i.e., north of the railway bridge, where the Chinese Boy Scouts camp, is the most dangerous. Snails infected with Japanese blood flukes are very likely to be present. During the great flood of 1931, snails from upstream ditches were washed into the river. These snails are not harmful in themselves, but unfortunately, they become infected with Japanese blood flukes through human waste and can then transmit the disease to people. As a member of the Western Yacht Club, I have informed the club's secretary-general, explaining the concerns about Qingyang Port. I am deeply concerned that Chinese and foreigners who come here to swim may become infected if they are not careful. Therefore, in addition to notifying Dr. Mierden, I am also reporting to you so that you can take appropriate action. If you permit, I plan to discuss schistosomiasis at the next meeting of the Municipal Public Health Club. If it is possible to discuss with the Boy Scout leaders to convene a Boy Scout group, our association is very willing to send a technician to give a lecture in Chinese. Furthermore, the Minhe bathhouse has been investigated and found to have no risk of such transmission. The Suzhou area is heavily infected. A few days ago, I took snails from a small river at the foot of Tiger Hill in Suzhou and verified that they had the same infection. A map is also attached. The Health Bureau, after receiving this letter, announced that "Japanese blood flukes" are common in Japan and the Jiangzhe provinces of our country. Blood flukes are small worms, the largest about an inch long, living in the blood vessels of the abdomen. Patients are often thin or have swollen abdomens, and severe cases can lead to death. The female worms lay eggs, which break through the blood vessels and enter the intestines, then are excreted in the feces. The small worms hatch from the eggs in the water and invade the snails, multiplying in their livers. They then leave the snail livers and live in the wet mud or on the leaves of plants. If they encounter someone walking barefoot, they will burrow into the body through the skin, settle in the blood vessels, and parasitize. The most important prevention method is to eliminate the snails. This can be done by adding one part of copper sulfate to 500,000 to 2,000,000 parts of water. After 48 hours, the snails will be killed. As for destroying the eggs, lime is more effective. Other methods include using disinfectants. All water from rivers should be disinfected with a one-in-ten-thousand solution of cresol. Other effective prevention methods include not swimming in the area and avoiding walking barefoot. However, Qingyang Port belongs to Kunshan, so the bureau cannot directly handle the matter. It has now sent a detailed letter to the relevant authorities in Kunshan, asking them to take appropriate measures.

After Half a Year of Marriage, Shi Mianchen's Wife Remains Alone 143

Claims to be Busy with Official Duties and Never Returns Home

After Much Inquiry, She Discovers He Has Someone Else

丨The Wife Sues for Divorce After Catching Him in Adultery丨

Lu Suzhen, a 31-year-old woman from Ningbo, resides at No. 217, Dean Lane, North Mountain West Road. On November 17th of last year, she married Shi Mianchen, a native of the same town, through a matchmaker. Shi is 35 years old and works at Guanshengyuan Confectionery. On the night of the wedding, Shi made an excuse to go out, leaving the bride unattended. Afterwards, although he occasionally returned home, he never stayed overnight. The couple never shared a bed, so after more than half a year, Lu is still a virgin. Lu found Shi's actions incomprehensible and repeatedly questioned him. Shi claimed to be too busy with official duties to return home. Lu found this excuse hard to believe, so she inquired in every possible way and finally learned that Shi had someone else. He was living with a widow named Zhou Wei at No. 15, Yiqing Lane, Yiqing Street, in the city. On the morning of February 10th of this year, at 7 a.m., Lu and her mother secretly went to catch them in adultery. They caught Shi and Zhou Wei in bed together. She called the police, who took the adulterous couple to the First Precinct of the Second District Public Security Bureau. They were released on bail. Because Shi had behaved in this way, Lu felt that it was difficult to continue living with him, so she retained lawyers Jiang Yiping and Wu Baotai to file a lawsuit in the First Special District Court, requesting (1) a divorce, (2) compensation for damages of 5,000 yuan, (3) a monthly living allowance of 50 yuan for three months during the litigation, and (4) payment of litigation costs. Upon receiving the lawsuit, Judge Luo Chongtai of the Special Court summoned them to the Fourth Civil Court yesterday. Shi Mianchen did not appear. After Lu Suzhen testified about what happened, the court said that personnel lawsuits require the defendant to be present for cross-examination. Since the defendant was not present, it was impossible to proceed with the trial. Furthermore, it was necessary to investigate the circumstances of the adultery with the First Precinct of the Second District. The case was adjourned and will be summoned again at a later date.

Feng Chengji, a 26-year-old from Changzhou, living at No. 33, Xinhua Lane, Pingliang Road, is still unmarried. Woman Jumps into the Sea Before Xinjiang Ship Enters Wusongkou Due to Worry About the Nation 154

Neither Economic Distress Nor Romantic Disappointment

Overstimulated by National Crisis Leading to This Last Resort

丨To Seek No Suffering, One Must Be in Another World丨

Yesterday, before the Xinjiang ship, which had sailed from Qingdao to Shanghai, entered Wusongkou, around one o'clock in the morning on the 21st, a woman jumped into the sea. Her companions discovered her suicide note and immediately reported it to the captain, who ordered the ship to reverse in an attempt to rescue her. However, due to the darkness and vastness of the sea, nothing could be done. It has been determined that the

Suicide Victim is Li Wenfang 155

Age 24, Cantonese. She worked as a female labor manager at the Provincial Silk Reeling Factory outside Wulinmen in Hangzhou for four years. She fled her home and ended up in Hangzhou because her grandmother forced her to become a concubine. On the train, she met Ms. Wen Ruihua, a student at the Agricultural College of Zhejiang University. Ms. Wen introduced her to Ms. Wei Qiongying, the secretary of the college, who then introduced her to the silk factory. Her monthly salary gradually increased from over twenty yuan to forty or fifty yuan. This time, during the factory's vacation, she took the opportunity to visit Ms. Wen in Nantong. She also had a friend, Ms. Luan Ruizhen, in Yantai who was about to go abroad to France. This friend had invited her to meet several times, so she especially invited Ms. Wen

To Accompany Her to Yantai for a Meeting 156

She traveled from Tongzhou by boat to Pukou and then took the Jinpu Railway to the Jiaoji Railway, arriving in Qingdao on the 18th. However, she changed her plans and did not go to Yantai. On the 19th, she accompanied Ms. Wen on the Xinjiang ship to Shanghai. According to Ms. Wen, the deceased was very happy during the trip and spent money generously, seeking comfort in transportation, lodging, food, and drink. After the fact, it was realized that she had undergone a major change, but no one expected this accident. In the letters left to her friends, she did not mention the cause of her death and instructed Ms. Wen to tell her other friends

To Falsely Claim She Died of Illness 157

To avoid social gossip. During her four years at the silk factory, she worked diligently and never made mistakes, so she was highly trusted by the factory director. She dressed simply and never had a boyfriend. However, because she had no parents and was all alone, she was always sad, even though she could support herself. Therefore, she liked to study Buddhist books and often read newspapers. In her conversations, she often lamented the evils of society and the failure of the nation. On the ship, she told Ms. Wen that it was not easy to be Chinese, nor was it easy to be Japanese. Even if one was born in America, there were other difficulties for Americans. To seek no suffering,

One Must Be in Another World 158

Etc. She did not die four years ago when she was destitute and helpless, but died today when she was self-sufficient and had no economic problems, nor was she heartbroken or disappointed. Judging from her words, she must have been overstimulated by the national crisis, which led to this last resort. The deceased was wearing a gray silk cotton robe, a blue short cloth shirt, a black short skirt, short hair, and gray Chen Jiageng sneakers. It is hoped that if a fisherman at sea finds her body, they can send a message to the Shanghai Jianghai Customs Lukiazui Water Police Station.

Continued Report on the Collision and Sinking of the He'an Ship 159

Markers Hung at the Sinking Site

Crew Members Discharged Yesterday with Compensation

Regarding the collision and sinking of the Hetai Company's He'an ship by the Norwegian merchant ship John Grieg Judson near the Guanghua Oil Fire Station in Gaoqiao on the morning of the 20th, yesterday was a Sunday, and the company was closed as usual. Therefore, negotiations will have to wait until today. Out of consideration for the crew members, the company first discharged them yesterday with compensation. The details obtained are recorded below.

Crew Members Discharged with Compensation 160

The ship had a load capacity of 1,100 tons and a crew of sixty-one, including the captain, chief mate, second mate, sailors, stokers, and stewards. After the ship sank, the crew and passengers were rescued by the Customs and the Asia Minor Steamship. The passengers immediately refunded their tickets. Yesterday afternoon, the crew members went to the Huang Yitai Longan Shop on Wai Xian Gua Street to request compensation from the Hetai Steamship Company. Mr. Huang, the manager, sympathized with the crew's plight and generously agreed to pay them not only their salary for this month but also an additional thirty yuan. The crew members expressed their satisfaction. At 6:30 PM, they gathered at the company, where the accountant called their names and distributed the severance pay. It is said that the ship had not been insured beforehand.

Port Police Protection 161

The He'an ship had a large hole in its port side, below the waterline, caused by the violent collision. The captain knew there was danger and immediately increased speed, steering towards the shallow waters of Pudong and dropping anchor. Therefore, the ship's condition yesterday remained the same as the day before. The Customs Port Police (i.e., the Water Police Station) dispatched four sampans and several police officers to guard the scene in shifts to prevent thieves. Although the ship sank in shallow water, it was in a key channel for entering and exiting the Huangpu River. To avoid danger, a red flag was hung there during the day, and a white and a green light were hung at night to warn ships to avoid the area.

Ticket Industry Association Holds Meeting 162

The Shanghai Steamship Passenger Ticket Industry Association received reports from its member associations stating that the losses suffered by passengers after the ship accident were enormous, and those missing were presumed to have drowned. To ensure the safety of passengers, the association convened a special executive committee meeting at 5 PM yesterday (the 21st) at No. 3 Antongli, Ximen. Zhu Ruiqing served as chairman, and Chen Buping served as secretary. After the chairman reported the purpose of the meeting, the discussion began, and the following resolutions were adopted: (1) That the Dalai Company's Yue Na ship negligently deviated from its route and sank the He'an ship, and that the shipping authorities should be requested to thoroughly investigate and severely punish them to ensure the safety of passengers. Resolution passed. (2) That a record of passenger losses should be kept to facilitate appeals and negotiations on their behalf. Resolution passed. (3) That the Customs authorities should be requested to increase inspections of all ships to avoid danger. Resolution passed. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the Shandong coast was sunny with northwest to northeast winds. The middle and lower reaches of the Yangtze River were cloudy, with heavy fog or drizzle in some areas. The wind was from the northeast to southeast. The coastal area south of Ma'an Island was cloudy with fog or localized showers, and the northeast wind was quite strong. Also, within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the temperature in Shanghai was 73.2 degrees Fahrenheit at the highest and 56.8 degrees Fahrenheit at the lowest. On the same day last year, the highest was 82.4 degrees Fahrenheit and the lowest was 62.6 degrees Fahrenheit.

Important Matter

Revised Customs Tariff Schedule (1) 167

Effective May 22

(Note)

If the standard of tax collection for each commodity specified in this tariff exceeds the standard, the tax will be levied on a pro rata basis.

The letters "n.o.p.f." in this tariff are abbreviations for "not otherwise provided for".

Notes for Categories 1, 2, 3, and 4

If piece goods or knitted fabrics contain multiple fibers, the composition of each fiber, if not more than 5% by weight, will not affect the classification of the tariff.

Cotton, linen, ramie, hemp, jute, and silk (mulberry silk or artificial silk) products that are sewn, edged, hemmed, or trimmed with other materials different from themselves will not affect the classification of the tariff.

For goods containing lace, ornaments, or other decorative materials, in addition to paying customs duties according to the tariff of the goods, an additional ad valorem tax of 5% should be levied.

Note for Category 4

The term "silk" in this tariff includes "artificial silk".

National Humiliation Week Speech by Mr. Huang Renzhi on My Views on the Future of Sino-Japanese Relations (Continued) 168

Third, there is unity. The Chinese population is several times larger than the Japanese, so why are we being invaded by the Japanese? Not only have some old national humiliations not been washed away in recent decades, but new national humiliations are increasing day by day. This is what Mr. Wang Yunwu said, that we Chinese are each a nation unto ourselves. Fourth, it is also what Mr. Wang Yunwu said, that everyone should act and not just talk emptily. We must resolve to act and each first do our duty well, and that is true action. I myself must work even harder, because this is working for the national crisis, and it must not be the same as in times of peace. Everyone's occupation is of course different, so just work hard from your own position. For example, I work at the Vocational Education Society. From now on, I must work doubly hard in my position. Normally I would rest after eight hours, but now and in the future, I must do extra work. Now I want to talk about Mr. Wang Yunwu again. He is the general manager of the Commercial Press. In the eyes of ordinary people, the general manager is like a general, who should be very happy, able to assign everything to others to do, and take leisure and comfort for himself. Why bother to work so hard? But Mr. Wang Yunwu is not like that. After the January 28th Incident, the Commercial Press suffered such huge losses, and yet it was able to recover in just half a year by August. What was the reason? It turns out that it was because Mr. Wang Yunwu was inside. When others wanted to rest, he didn't rest. Even on weekends and holidays, when he should have sought some entertainment, he didn't go. Even when people invited him to banquets and various gatherings, he didn't go. He endured all kinds of pain and led his colleagues to work hard. Where there is a will, there is a way. The Commercial Press was able to recover in half a year. How much we should admire the spirit of Mr. Wang Yunwu. Therefore, starting tomorrow, we should all learn from him, and China will have hope.

It is a pity that today's audience is all ordinary people. If there were some government officials here today, after hearing Mr. Wang Yunwu's spirit of hard work, if those officials were also willing to take responsibility for national affairs and work in this way, revitalizing China would not be difficult at all. What I have said is all old news. Now I will say a few new words, because many gentlemen have already spoken on this topic. I am here today to bring it to a close, and I hope that everyone will keep it in their minds and truly act on it, and not just talk emptily.

The most important thing for China now is to change its attitude towards life. But how to change it? We must first recognize what a person is, because now everyone only sees an "I", and only sees the "small self" and not the "big self". That is, people's concept of themselves is wrong. Usually, people only know that their hands, feet, muscles, and skin are their own, and that is a "small self". We should understand that this is not me, that many people are me, and that all of China is me. Furthermore, there is a soul beyond the physical body. Only when the physical body and the soul are combined is there a true me.

You can see from the newspapers about a recent incident. In the French Concession, there was a barber soliciting business on the roadside. A police officer went up to check his license, and the barber was so frightened that he tried to escape. But the police officer chased after him and kicked him several times, killing him. If this happened in a foreign country, it would be a big problem. Unfortunately, it happened in China. Many people watched the excitement, but few offered help. Therefore, in recent years, I have been greatly stimulated. I once had a friend, Mr. Shen Pengnian, who was riding in a rickshaw on Avenue du Père Froc and was hit by a truck carrying goods. Mr. Shen was thrown more than ten feet from the rickshaw and died instantly. But you can imagine that Avenue du Père Froc is a very busy road, and of course few people saw the accident. But everyone was afraid of trouble and stood by without asking. At that time, a Westerner happened to pass by on his motorcycle. Seeing the truck causing the accident and fleeing, he was dissatisfied, so he chased after it, copied down the license plate number, and testified. Therefore, although Mr. Shen died, it was still possible to negotiate because of the help of the foreigner. Isn't this an extremely painful thing? There was another incident last year when my son saw a police officer beating a rickshaw puller on the road. He went up to copy down the officer's number. When the officer saw my son copying down his number, he started to beat him. My son questioned him, saying that if the rickshaw puller violated the regulations, he could be taken to the police station or punished according to the law. Why beat him like this? The officer not only ignored him but also took my son to the police station. Coincidentally, there was a woman nearby, only in her twenties, but she was very courageous and secretly followed to testify. As a result, the officer was punished, and my son and the woman were released. At that time, I said to my son that this was the right thing to do. Many people who stand by and watch are mistaken in their view of life, thinking that their own body is me, and that the rickshaw puller who is being beaten by the police officer is from Jiangbei and has nothing to do with me. They keep chanting "compatriots" in words, but in reality, they are unrelated. But we should know what the meaning of the word "compatriot" is. We should know that a compatriot is a metaphor for being born from the same womb and being closely related to each other, meaning they are one and the same. Unexpectedly, now great love is only regarded as a slogan. I think that the people of China now see that their compatriots in the Northeast are suffering in deep water and hot fire, while those in the South can be at ease and carefree. If this time Japan was invaded by the Soviet Union to Hokkaido, I am afraid that the whole country would be excited to the point of madness, and would never again be like China, where they are still fighting for power and profit and internal strife continues. What I have said above is about people. Now I want to talk about life, "life" being the opposite of death. Only by not fearing death can one live enough. There are also sayings like "seek life in death" and "escape from death", which means not fearing death. For example, everyone is here listening to a lecture. Suddenly, a bomb comes, but it falls here and has not yet exploded. If everyone has no way and is afraid of death, then after a scramble, the bomb may explode, and will everyone still be able to live? If someone is not afraid of death and is willing to die himself to remove the bomb, then hundreds of people will be able to live. If everyone is unwilling to die and wants to live, they will all perish together. We know that the 19th Route Army last year was not foolish, because they thought that if we died in places like Miaohang and Jiangwan, everyone could survive. So our survival now is bought with the blood of many soldiers last year. We must not forget!

We now, whether we have read books or studied sociology, and have some common sense, should all know that the armies of the past, like holding a white flag to recruit soldiers, saying how much money a month, everyone is unwilling to go, what does it mean, because this is a deception and has no true meaning, now someone to join the volunteer army, is that could have not died, but for the country to die, the nation can survive, it is worth dying, could have not gone to the army, for the nation to fight, can fight for the nation's survival, it is also worth being a soldier,

I have been greatly stimulated recently, and I ask myself that living in peace in the South is truly guilty in my heart, so I hope everyone recognizes "life", the last sentence, nothing more than to change the attitude of life, and from tomorrow onwards, I myself should also change, to not be ashamed of being a part of the nation, from then on, I am willing to share with you all,

Paradise 169

— Hua Ling

Zhabei was beaten to a pulp by the Imperial Army, and the flames of the explosions soared into the sky. The Concession foreigners, enjoying themselves with their wives and concubines, ascended to the eighteenth floor to admire the greatest fire in Shanghai's history. This was a scene from the Battle of Shanghai last year.

Yes, in Shanghai, there is "British territory" and "French territory". Although Zhabei has become a "no-man's land", the Japanese soldiers in the Concession dare not act wildly. That's why the Concession is so popular.

These few days, Tianjin and Beijing are somewhat unstable. "Antiques are valuable, the rich are next, and land is light." So, antiques that have been swept away have been transported to the "French territory" of Shanghai for safekeeping. After the antiques were transported, the rich people of Tianjin and Beijing, with their wives and concubines, packing their belongings, took trains or ships to the south. According to reports, various hotels in Shanghai are booming these days, which proves that the Shanghai Concession is truly a "paradise" on earth.

Originally, Shanghai was already crowded with inland officials who were fleeing from soldiers and bandits, plus politicians who had stepped down from power and disappointed soldiers since the twelfth year of the Republic. Although the Concession has been expanding, and the buildings have been built like pavilions, if people from Tianjin and Beijing continue to come to Shanghai to enjoy themselves, "paradise" will inevitably suffer from overcrowding.

The war in North China has a tendency to spread south. Those wealthy gentlemen in North China outside of Tianjin and Beijing, who have not yet been oppressed by domestic soldiers and bandits to come to Shanghai, may join the group of "prospering Shanghai" in the near future. By then, it will be terrible, "paradise" will be squeezed and broken.

The Japanese have already planned for us there. They want to "join hands" with the foreigners living in Shanghai to create a "permanently peaceful" "free city" and expand the Concession to Wusong, Jiangwan, Zhenru, and Zhabei.

Wonderful! Once this matter becomes a reality, Shanghai will not become the "world's largest paradise"? Haha, manage it well, and it will happen soon. Please don't rush, wait and see.

Lantern Disaster 170

— Qing Qu

This time, our Jiading, although a small county, has continuously produced its lanterns. At first, it was the four villages, making noise every night, with gongs and drums beating loudly. People who went out of the city to watch the lanterns were like a tide, and the county magistrate and district chiefs turned a deaf ear and let them run wild! Some people said that they were occupied by Japanese soldiers for more than two months last year, and they were slaves to the county. But after a year, have everyone forgotten this bitter day? Bah! This is called "making fun in hardship." A few ignorant scholars put on Western suits and leather shoes and ran around in the countryside for a week, and then wrote articles complaining about "rural bankruptcy" and "economic decline" and published them in the newspaper to complain for them. It's really like scratching an itch from outside the boot, how can they know how much money they spend on the lanterns with blood and sweat and mud?

Right now, Loutang Town is also doing this job. It is heard that a certain district chief wanted to prohibit it, and he insisted on the matter with his own job, good! Coincidentally, he encountered the lantern-loving gentlemen, so you went to Suzhou to get the costumes, you donated two large loads of candles, and you went to fight with a certain district chief. So the lanterns of Loutang can be regarded as being stimulated. In fact, is the lantern thing really needed locally? Or should it be prohibited? If this question is raised to be resolved, isn't it going to be laughable? Later, the two leaders were indeed taken to the official office to be sued. Unexpectedly, someone was covering the two behind them. You can keep them locked in the detention center, I will send them food to eat, and I will buy them things to use, because of this, the lawsuit is a lawsuit, the lanterns are still being put out. The word "prohibited" has simply been declared bankrupt in the government.

But in the city, the people who agree with the lanterns are also somewhat itchy and unbearable, saying that since the villages can put out lanterns, why should the city prohibit it? So they also started to put out lanterns, calling it "celebrating the victory of the war". Who knows, the sky has wind and clouds, and people have good and bad fortune. Before the lanterns were put out, a tragedy was staged. Several people who took the stage were beaten with their heads broken and bleeding, and they had to go to Kunshan to ask Mr. Min's family for help, and at that time, I don't know how many people gathered at the second gate of the county government and fought with the police. It's really like a full martial arts performance in Jiaxing Prefecture. Finally, tomorrow it will form a state of strike, sparing no effort to make a fuss, almost more powerful than dealing with diplomatic failures, and overthrowing Cao Lu Zhang. The county chamber of commerce held an emergency meeting and proposed six of the most effective protest letters. What a Xu Weizhen county magistrate, calm in attitude, not anxious, and accepted every one of them. Coincidentally, four robbers came to the Qia Tai Egg Bank outside the Rainbow Bridge west of the west gate and robbed more than four hundred yuan in silver dollars. It was eight o'clock in the evening, and the meeting had not yet ended. The people present heard the alarm on the phone and were shocked, and they seemed to realize that the lanterns in the city were not a peaceful thing?

Wu Zhihui's Military Cap 171

— Yang Yusheng

In the seventeenth year of the Republic of China, Wuhan was in the period of splitting the Communists, Mr. Wu Zhihui and Mr. Wang Jingwei had occasional differences in political views and had a big ink lawsuit.

Among the many sophisticated and slippery articles, I still remember that Mr. Wu had taught in Tangshan before. And I still remember that he once said these few words to Mr. Wang:

"Now, if we put two military caps on our heads, the national affairs will have a way."

Oh! Because Mr. Wu and Mr. Wang did not wear military caps, the national affairs have no way. It is said that Tangshan has been lost again. No, it's a full retreat. Then, it's probably a new plan. Now, the time when all the people of China, whether they are foolish old people or rude teenagers, must wear military caps, if China is still considered a country, it will probably come soon! I earnestly ask Mr. Wu to put on a military cap first and advocate for the world! We should unite to support Mr. Wu's military cap doctrine, and the national crisis can be saved.

Quick Record of a Rainstorm 172

— Huang Yingdai

These days it has suddenly become very hot, although it is not June, the temperature is already very high, it is very good to use ice cream Dutch water as a heat-relieving drink.

Coming back from the sun-drenched road, I felt a little dizzy in my head. I wanted to do some work, but my body fell onto the bed and I had a good dream and entered dreamland.

Two hours later, a few claps of thunder woke me up from my good dream. I got up and saw that dark clouds had filled the surroundings. I knew it was going to rain heavily. Soon, raindrops like soybeans came flying. At this time, standing at the window and looking at the road, there were many special scenes that could be used as material for writing articles.

A sister-in-law across the street, seeing the raindrops, ran to the balcony to grab the clothes and diapers drying in the window.

The pedestrians on the road were all running for their lives, but the raindrops were too big. Even if you ran two or three steps in the raindrops, your clothes would be soaked.

The rickshaw pullers saw it raining on the way and immediately put up the cloth awnings for the passengers, but none of them brought raincoats themselves, they just ran wildly in the rain, not afraid of the cold rain.

Only the car is the most stable, no matter how thick the raindrops are, it can't hit the car window, it won't make the clothes of the people in the car wet at all.

When a young couple was walking hand in hand, the raindrops suddenly hit them, and they ran quickly to a shop to avoid the rain, but they were afraid of missing the time to watch the movie, a naive prank?

Many women, in small houses, were really too hot to live in, and took their short benches and ran to the alley to cool off, but a burst of rain drove them all back home.

A deafening thunderclap fell from the sky, scaring the lady next door to open her mouth and keep chanting "Amitabha", her psychology only hoped that the black-hearted people would be struck by lightning.

Half an hour of rainstorm passed in haste, the sun still escaped from the dark clouds in the west, the street was the same as just now, except for the road surface covered with rainwater wet situation, pedestrians also restored the hustle and bustle before the storm, the sky is still very hot, but it is still reduced by three points of heat.

Chapter Seven: A Few Words Sever Affection, Close the Door and Weep, One Shoulder Carries Righteousness, Toast Wine and Discuss

When Gui Zhi said this, his voice was hard, and he couldn't say anything. He turned around and went home. After arriving home, it happened that his mother was not at home. He closed the door, lay down on the pit, held a big pillow in both hands, and cried. He didn't know why, he was so sad that he hugged the pillow tightly and just kept crying. After a while, Jiang Min came back from the backyard, and outside the house, he heard Gui Zhi's whimpering. At first, he was taken aback. When he walked into the house, the bedroom door was tightly closed. He pushed it twice, but the door didn't open. Jiang thought, this is strange. In the first month of the year, I have not said anything to him, and no one has offended him, why is he crying like this? So he pounded on the door and said: Hey! Open the door, child, what's wrong with you? When Gui Zhi was crying, he just wanted to cry out in one breath and vent the anger in his chest. As for whether anyone heard it, he didn't consider this. At this time, the two doors were pounding, and he suddenly thought that if he cried so loudly, wouldn't his mother ask for a reason? Now that his mother is here, should he stop crying or not? If he stops, he can stop crying at will, and crying would be unreasonable. If he doesn't stop, closing the two doors tightly and making his mother not know what to do will scare her. He was lying on the pit and couldn't think of a proper idea for a while, but he cried even harder. Jiang pounded on the door and said: What's wrong? What's wrong? Open the door and tell me clearly. As he said, he pounded the door a few times. Seeing that the door could not be opened, he said: You open the door or not, if you don't open the door, I will go to the backyard and ask Company Commander Zhao to come and beat down this door. Gui Zhi heard that Company Commander Zhao was going to be asked to beat down the door, which was related to face. First, he didn't open the door, jumped up on the bed and replied: Are you crazy? Why did you bring outsiders here? Jiang said: You child, you are really crazy, open your mouth and scold people, even scolding me. Gui Zhi didn't say anything more, jumped up and opened the door, then turned around and lay on the pit again, facing the corner of the wall, and didn't say anything. (Seventy-seven)

Women's Paradise

Housewife's Must Know 174

— Chu

(1) Buying Rice and Cooking

The white rice we eat every day is mostly washed several times during cooking, but if the first-class fine rice is rubbed and washed by hand, the cooked rice will not only be useless to eat, but will also be harmful. Why? When we cook fine rice into cooked rice, we use scientific methods to test its nutritional value, which is very low. That is: (1) White rice has lost vitamins A and B. (2) It lacks protein, especially the amino acids necessary for maintaining life. Because of elimination, the body is fatally struck. (3) The potassium and phosphorus in inorganic salts are increased, while iron, iodine, etc. are washed away. Therefore, when we eat this kind of white rice, we only have calories, and the necessary nutrients for the body and the nutrients necessary for maintaining normal life are insufficient. Moreover, when vitamin B is lacking, the body will feel uncomfortable. We Chinese people, who generally do not have knowledge about eating white rice, often think that eating first-class fine rice is good, and the more rice is washed, the cleaner it is. You must know that fine rice is already lacking in nutrients, and if you desperately rub and wash it, then all the nutrients will be completely lost. Please pay special attention to this point, housewives. Now I will explain in detail the reasons for the loss of nutrients:

(1) Loss of nutrients in fine rice: From unhulled brown rice, after pounding, it becomes fine white rice. The lost ingredients are fat (73.9%), crude fiber (67.3%), ash (41.2%). The phosphoric acid in the ash reduces its composition in proportion to the pounding time. Especially because of prolonged pounding, inorganic salts, proteins, and vitamin A are completely lost. Now health experts advocate brown rice movement, which is for the sake of maintaining the original nutrients.

(2) Loss of nutrients during washing: Ordinary second-class white rice roughly contains vitamin B. If it is washed and rubbed, then vitamin B will also disappear due to its water-soluble nature. Other crude fibers are lost by 76.4%, fat by 61.6%, and ash by 41.8%. Judging from this, the rice we eat every day should not be too fine, and should not be washed too much. Moreover, when washing, do not rub it by hand. Wash it lightly once or twice. If we only eat first-class fine rice and wash the rice five or six times during cooking, then we will develop beriberi in one or two months, and at the same time, our complexion will gradually become withered and yellow.

(2) Testing Drinking Water

In cities with perfect water systems, the water you eat is certainly not dangerous, but in rural areas and places without water systems, most of them are drawn from rivers and wells, so housewives should understand the quality of the water. Now I will introduce a simple method for testing the composition of water quality:

(1) Silver nitrate test method: Fill a glass with drinking water, add five or six drops of silver nitrate solution, and it will turn light white. This water can be used. If the white color becomes turbid and has precipitation, it is dirty water, and it must have excrement and urine mixed in it. This is proof that the water contains salt. However, wells and streams close to the coast also have saline water, and although there is no excrement and urine flowing in, it will also become turbid. Of course, we can determine this by observing the surrounding conditions and the normal properties of the water.

(2) Organic matter test method: Add sulfuric acid and potassium permanganate solution (0.1%) two or three drops to half a cup of water, and the water will heat up and turn purple-red. If the purple-red color does not disappear, it proves that there is no organic matter in the water and it can be drunk. If the purple-red color disappears immediately, add twelve or three drops of the above-mentioned medicine to test, and it is still the same, then it is determined that the water must contain a large amount of decaying matter of animal and plant origin.

(3) Ammonia test method: Add four or five drops of Nessler's reagent to half a cup of water. If there is ammonia in the water, it will turn light yellow or reddish-brown according to the amount. If there is something precipitated in the reddish-brown color, then the water is even more dirty.

The Secondary School Federation Was Established Yesterday 177

▲Initiating the Organization of the National Federation of Middle School Students

The Shanghai Municipal Secondary School Student Federation has been inactive since the January 28th Shanghai Incident. Considering the severity of the national crisis, it is necessary to reorganize to bolster national salvation efforts. The Twenty-Sixth Anniversary of Tongji University 178

▲President Weng Zhilong Outlines Future Development Plans

The National Tongji University in Wusong held its twenty-sixth-anniversary celebration yesterday, an event of great prominence. President Dr. Weng Zhilong presided over the ceremony, recounting the university's past history and outlining seven future development plans: (1) To establish a College of Science to comply with the regulations; (2) To add a second teaching hospital to increase student internship opportunities; (3) To construct an industrial museum for reference and research; (4) To expedite the construction of a library to add reference books; (5) To build a gymnasium to promote physical education; (6) To establish a second affiliated middle school to increase the source of university students; (7) To expand the affiliated machinist school and convert it into a higher vocational school. The Provisional Emergency Council Meeting of the Middle School Teachers' Federation Was Held Yesterday 179

▲Discussing Measures to Save the North China Crisis

▲Telegraphing the National Government to Oppose Russia's Sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway

▲Visiting the Russian Envoy This Morning to Present a Letter of Opinion

In light of the fall of the Northeast and the crisis in North China, the Shanghai Middle School Teachers' Federation convened a provisional emergency council meeting yesterday to discuss salvage measures. The details are recorded as follows:

▲Council Meeting: Held at the Lianhuan Society at 8 a.m., attended by all council members. The presidium consisted of Chen Jicheng, Wu Zhiqian, and Sheng Xugong, with Xu Zexiang recording. Key resolutions: (1) Regarding the case of how to salvage the situation in Northeast and North China, resolved: (A) To send a telegram to the national populace and various organizations, urging them to pay attention to the seriousness of the situation. (B) For this Federation to initiate and convene a joint conference of various organizations in the city to discuss measures and issue a declaration. Wu Zhiqian, Wu Zhenjin, Song Binqin, Huang Yan, Liu Tianan, Ma Zhongkai, and Guo Ping were appointed as representatives of this Federation to liaise with various sectors, convened by Liu Zirun. (C) This Federation's opinions on the situation will be submitted to the joint conference for resolution. (2) The case of the Federation holding an anti-Japanese speech week, taking turns to speak at various schools every week, resolved and passed. (3) To send letters to various schools, urging them to quickly organize student unions and intensify anti-Japanese work, resolved and passed. (4) To send letters to various schools, urging them to step up military training and first aid training, resolved and passed. (5) The case of the Federation sending personnel to various schools to give speeches in commemoration of the May 30th Incident, resolved and passed. (6) The case of organizing a committee to inspect goods to avoid purchasing enemy goods, resolved and passed. (7) To request the Municipal Government to announce aviation donations and expedite the purchase of aircraft with the donations already received, resolved to be handed over to the standing council to send a letter to the Municipal Government.

▲Telegram to the National Government: The Federation sent a telegram to the National Government opposing Russia's sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway, which read: "To the esteemed National Government in Nanjing, it has been widely rumored that Soviet Russia will sell the Chinese Eastern Railway to Japan. Furthermore, according to a Reuters dispatch from Moscow, a statement by Soviet Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov indicates that this matter has become an undeniable fact. The sovereignty of the Chinese Eastern Railway belongs to both China and Russia, as clearly stipulated in the Sino-Soviet Agreement. The Soviet Russian government, without obtaining our country's consent, dares to disregard the great injustice of the world, violate the agreement, and unilaterally sell the railway to the bellicose and brutal Japan. This association swears to oppose this act of contempt for good faith and infringement upon our sovereignty. Therefore, we hereby telegraph to your government, requesting that a strong protest be lodged with Soviet Russia immediately to uphold public opinion and safeguard our sovereignty. The telegram is urgent. The Shanghai Middle School Teachers' Federation bows.

▲Visiting the Russian Envoy Today: The Federation has decided to dispatch three representatives, Li Yongzhong, Shen Zurun, and Liu Zirun, to visit the Russian envoy this morning and present a letter of opinion opposing the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway. The letter has been translated into Russian and is recorded below: "To Whom It May Concern, It has been widely rumored recently that your government will sell the Chinese Eastern Railway to Japan. According to a Reuters dispatch from Moscow, your Foreign Minister Litvinov has issued a statement indicating that this matter will become a reality. The sovereignty of the Chinese Eastern Railway is stipulated in Article 9, Section 5 of the 1924 Sino-Soviet Agreement as belonging to both the Republic of China and the Soviet Union. Therefore, the disposition of the railway cannot be carried out unilaterally by any country without the consent of both China and Russia. This is a legal imperative. Moreover, at a time when China and Russia are seeking friendship, and the people of both countries are looking forward to working together to promote peace in the Far East, your country intends to disregard the great injustice of the world and violate the agreement. This has deeply surprised and saddened our entire country, both government and public. Considering the importance of this matter, this Federation has specially appointed three representatives, Liu Zirun, Shen Zurun, and Li Yongzhong, to visit Your Excellency the Ambassador and convey everything in person. We respectfully request an audience for your convenience."
