The Ministry of Education Stipulates Enrollment Methods for Various Universities 182

▲To Be Implemented From the Twenty-Second Academic Year ▲To Cultivate a Majority of Practical Science Talents

In previous years, domestic universities and colleges had no restrictions on the enrollment of new students. The quantitative proportion of students in liberal arts and law, etc., to those in agriculture, engineering, medicine, and science could not be balanced, leading to the contradictory phenomenon of a surplus and shortage of talent. The Ministry of Education yesterday specially stipulated the enrollment methods for various universities and colleges for the twenty-second academic year and issued an order to comply, making fundamental corrections. The original order stated:

"University education is originally intended to research advanced academics and cultivate specialized talents. However, China's millennia-old tradition of valuing literature and neglecting the practical has become deeply ingrained. Scholars have taken this as their orientation, and liberal arts and law, etc., are simpler to establish. Those who run schools often choose the easy path, leading to a focus on the humanities and a neglect of production, forming a contradictory phenomenon of a surplus and shortage of talent. According to the Ministry's statistics for the twentieth academic year, liberal arts students nationwide (i.e., the colleges and departments listed under Category A below) accounted for 70 percent, reaching 23,230 people, while practical science students (i.e., the colleges and departments listed under Category B below) accounted for 30 percent, totaling 9,928 people. This proportion cannot but be regarded as an abnormal development, lacking balance, and urgently needing correction. Now that foreign aggression is increasing daily and the national economy is declining to an extreme, a majority of practical science talents must be cultivated to meet the extraordinary environment and social needs. Since the beginning of this month, the Ministry has repeatedly received directives from the Central Authorities to strictly reform, and orders have already been issued for compliance. As the twenty-second academic year is about to begin, the enrollment of new students in various universities and colleges should be carefully considered and restricted to conform to the purpose of correcting the abnormal development of liberal arts education. The specific enrollment methods for each school and college are stipulated as follows: (1) From this year onward, any university that operates both Category A colleges (Colleges of Literature, Law, Commerce, Education, Arts, etc.) and Category B colleges (Colleges of Science, Agriculture, Medicine, Engineering, etc.) must ensure that the number of new students enrolled in any Category A college, including transfer students, does not exceed the number of new students enrolled in any Category B college. If the number of departments established in Category A colleges differs from the number of departments established in Category B colleges, the average number of new students enrolled in each department of any Category A college must not exceed the average number of new students enrolled in each department of any Category B college. (2) From this year onward, any independent college that operates both Category A departments (Departments of Literature, Law, Commerce, Education, Arts, etc.) and Category B departments (Departments of Science, Agriculture, Medicine, Engineering, etc.) must ensure that the number of new students enrolled in any Category A department, including transfer students, does not exceed the number of new students enrolled in any Category B department. If the number of departments established in Category A departments differs from the number of departments established in Category B departments, the average number of new students enrolled in each department of any Category A department must not exceed the average number of new students enrolled in each department of any Category B department. (3) The number of new students enrolled in independent colleges that only operate Category A departments as described above must not exceed the number of new students enrolled in each such college in the twentieth academic year. If there are special circumstances, they must be submitted to the Ministry for approval in advance. (4) The Ministry will not review the qualifications for admission of new students at any school that does not strictly adhere to these regulations, or further corrective measures will be taken. The above regulations, except for colleges that exclusively admit female students, which are temporarily not applicable, and those with separate orders, shall be uniformly followed by all national, provincial, and registered private universities and colleges. This order is hereby issued for the said universities, colleges, and bureaus to forward it to provincial and registered private universities and colleges for compliance. This order."

▲Escaping a Penalty Kick: Zhang Longhai hugged the ball and entered the field. The entire audience stood in solemn silence. Shenbao, in the south, first launched a northern expedition. Chenbao's rear defense was in a state of chaos. Hu Zongfan blocked the stone frame on the left, Xu Zexiang risked half his life, and Zhou Fuming suffered both his legs. Fortunately, relying on the blessings of his ancestors, no major disaster occurred within the house. Sun Daosheng's precious saber was not old, and his ambition was everything, but he was unfamiliar with his partner, losing many good opportunities. He could only sigh to the sky, "Heaven will destroy me, not a sin of war."

It is said that the six newspaper armies, after meeting and fighting fiercely at the baseball field on the afternoon of the 20th, continued their battle at the Municipal Stadium yesterday. ▲ A Winter Melon Appears - As soon as the battle drums sounded, the two armies rushed to compete. The opponents were all young lads with good leg strength. Although our side consisted of veteran soldiers, they were physically strong, tall and short, fat and thin, of all sizes. Qian Hua, the "winter melon" with a large belly (as named by the Da Mei Evening News), attracted the most attention from the audience. Every step and every move caused his entire body to shake, making the viewers burst into laughter.

▲ Behind-the-Scenes Stories - Captain Sun Daosheng skillfully maneuvered the ball on his feet, performing excellently, but unfortunately, he fell to the ground and injured his left hand. Veteran Xie Hong, with his copper skin and iron bones, bravely resisted in every battle, making outstanding contributions. Forward Zhu Mingxin charged through the bloody path, covered in sweat, constantly complaining. Lu Erqiang displayed the true colors of a scholar, but he was as light as a swallow and the fastest on his feet. Jiang Huaiqing saved a penalty kick and returned the favor. Huang Jiping, tall and strong, shot a ball high into the air for five minutes, flipping a back somersault, causing the entire field to burst into laughter. Although our newspaper did not win this match, the united effort and spirit were truly outstanding.

An Overview of Medicine and Pharmacy in Shanghai in the Past Decade (Continued) 194

— Pang Jingzhou

Chapter 4: Business Conditions

Section 3: Quack Doctors and Fake Medicines

The term "quack doctor" should not, in principle, be a specialized term. However, in the current reality of Shanghai, unfortunately, there are many people who treat patients who neither base their practice on traditional medicine nor possess genuine knowledge of modern medicine. They can only be reluctantly called "quack doctors." In certain societies, quack doctors take advantage of shallow public knowledge and economic decline to practice so-called "jianghu" (roving) techniques, allowing their businesses to flourish. Five or six years ago, there were already "trauma and dental doctors" who pushed large carts with cloth canopies, also "selling" so-called German Lion Brand 914, etc. However, they are now outdated because social understanding is also progressing, albeit superficially. Therefore, current quack doctors have rented suitable premises in bustling areas, installed bright red electric lights, and set up small exhibitions of venereal disease specimens along the roadside, posting large advertisements in newspapers filled with old and new medical terms and charitable slogans. Thus, their business has gradually infiltrated the middle and upper classes from the lowest levels of society. The prices they charge have also gradually increased due to the patronage of the middle and upper classes. From swindling for food to wanting to get rich is also an inevitable trend of human nature. However, medicines are ultimately tools for treating diseases, and diagnosis is the knowledge of doctors. Quack doctors can advertise things like "Olenmei needle, one yuan each" or "Aerti gong, seven jiao each" in newspapers. Then why can't Feng Cunren and Qing Yu Tang also advertise loudly, saying "Xiaochuan lian, two jiao and a half per qian" or "Jinwen rhubarb, three jiao and a half per liang," and use this as a slogan for solving social and economic medical problems? This ridiculous spectacle not only fails to elicit correction from society but is even sympathized with by some gentry. The state of affairs in China is therefore predictable. In the old days of conservatism, weapons were only spears and halberds, which everyone could own. Now, guns and cannons are sharp and dangerous, so people are not allowed to privately possess firearms. However, letting new chemical products fall into the hands of the unlearned and unskilled is probably more likely to kill than to save. Moreover, when new drugs kill, there is no proof of wrongdoing. The ignorant authorities still adhere to ancient versions of "The Washing Away of Wrongs." (I once saw a lawyer write an article strongly refuting forensic autopsies and advocating "The Washing Away of Wrongs.") Even if a lawsuit is filed, it is impossible to find a suitable charge. Why do government authorities only know how to ban firearms and not know how to regulate the use of drugs?

Once, I was blamed by a friend for saying that the prosperity of modern medicine and the proliferation of Western drugs have created so many strange phenomena and that we should bear some responsibility for correcting them. So, my first step was to blame Western merchants for supplying drugs to quack doctors. However, the Western merchant replied well. He said that your country has many kinds of "healing craftsmen," and it is not known which ones should buy our medicines and which ones should not. There are no clear regulations to date. We are people of a rule-of-law country, and without legal basis, we cannot be held responsible for others! I had to retreat in silence.

In the pharmaceutical world...the opposite of quack doctors are fake medicines. The source of fake medicines can be said to be Shanghai. According to newspapers, there are not only so-called "scientific methods" and "carefully researched products," but also famous mountains and rivers in the inland, and various magical herbs, all of which are transported to Shanghai to save people. It can be considered a great blessing for Shanghai residents that the place of origin is not as important as the place of gathering. But then again, what kind of grass root or tree bark cannot be used as medicine? There is no such thing as genuine or fake in itself. But if the actual effect is too far from the advertising and the substance is greatly contrary to the theory, then it is a fake product. The production of fake products can be divided into two types. One is a single-recipe herbal remedy without efficacy statistics, and the other is a speculative product that uses excuses to collect money. The former is less harmful, while the latter is intentional and despicable. Since the discovery of "San Na Xing that mistreats tuberculosis" and "Wuliang Shou that is neither donkey nor horse (saying that electricity is added to ginseng, etc.)" last year, I feel that San Na Xing is enough to delay the early treatment of tuberculosis, and Wuliang Shou is misleading and manipulating people's minds by playing with academic theories. Therefore, I once wrote an article in the Social Medical Journal severely criticizing their absurdities. However, as a result, the two companies filed lawsuits against me, accusing me of damaging their reputation. Finally, after a real drug test and research, it was proved that they were all kinds of fallacies, and this case gradually subsided.

Thoughts After Hearing the Will of Yu Ziwei of Yongjia to Dissect the Corpse 195

— Ji Jilin

Yongjia has been opened as a commercial port since the late Qing Dynasty, and it has been more than sixty years now. In this era of increasingly advanced society, relying on the driving force of nature and human beings, all phenomena, such as politics, economy, and education, have made considerable progress. The scientific new medical cause is naturally no exception. Recently, in the vigorous new medical circle, an exciting and sensational event has occurred. The occurrence of this event has a great impact on society and has contributed a lot to the new medical circle. The fact is this.

Yu Ziwei was a pioneer in the medical circles of Japan. He was the father of Professor Yu Desun of Hangzhou Medical and Pharmaceutical College. Mr. Yu had in-depth research in both Chinese and Western medicine, and was particularly proficient in anatomy. He spared no effort in encouraging younger generations. Last year, he suffered from stomach cancer. Knowing that he would not recover, he left a will to dissect his body.

Death is the last stage of life, which no one can avoid. If viewed from a philosophical perspective, it is a very ordinary thing. Moreover, corpse dissection has long been "commonplace" in Europe and the United States. However, in this aimless Chinese society, especially in Yongjia, when people have not yet recognized the true value of scientific medicine, Mr. Yu's ability to set an example and advocate dissection is therefore considered a meaningful and commendable thing.

Dissection has been practiced in ancient China. According to ancient books, the Book of Documents records "removing the fetus from a pregnant woman" and "cutting off the legs of those who wade in the morning, and dissecting the hearts of virtuous people." The Book of Han records the biography of Wang Mang, saying that "Zhai Yi's party, Wang Sunqing, was captured. Mang ordered the chief physician Shangfang and Kao Tu to dissect him together, measuring his five viscera, and guiding his meridians with bamboo mats to know their end." But this was driven by a kind of curiosity, making occasional observations, without any medical significance. As for dissection for the purpose of medical research, it already existed in the Yellow Emperor's era. The anatomical knowledge recorded in the Inner Canon and Ling Shu chapters all came from "dissection and observation." Unfortunately, the dissection at that time was simple, so many ancient Chinese medical books contain erroneous anatomical knowledge. Even the Classic of Difficulties, written by Bian Que, who was revered as a medical saint in later generations, is not exempt. For example, the Classic of Difficulties records that "the lungs weigh three catties and three liang, with six lobes and two ears, totaling eight lobes," and "the heart weighs twelve liang, with seven holes and three hairs in the middle, holding three he of essence and sweat," etc., which are completely derived from conjecture. However, this is not to blame the ancients, because science was not developed thousands of years ago, so it is certainly impossible to be as precise as it is today. It is only a pity that later generations of doctors did not continue to study and verify, and the errors in ancient books are still regarded as golden rules and cannot be corrected. Even more so, they have become increasingly exaggerated, causing this erroneous anatomical knowledge to spread among the people. This time, when Mr. Yu's body was dissected, representatives of various legal groups and the public were notified separately to observe publicly, fundamentally correcting the public's misconceptions about anatomy. Medicine is one of science, and its foundation is built on anatomy. Therefore, the public's correct understanding of anatomy is the beginning of understanding scientific medicine.

Countries famous for medicine in the world all attach great importance to anatomy. For example, the Institute of Anatomy at the University of Berlin in Germany was established in 1713 AD. Hundreds of corpses are placed in the practice room for students to study. Since the reform of our country, the new medical cause has also shown a prosperous atmosphere. However, anatomy is still rare. Medical schools, except for national and public schools, can extract prisoners or death row inmates from prisons with government assistance for dissection. As for private medical schools, they can only run wildly among the villages and wild graves, seeking exposed bones as practice materials. The reason why there are not many corpse dissections in our country is not because there is a lack of experienced pathological anatomy experts, but because of the opposition of the people. The public is influenced by the ancient訓of "the body, hair, and skin are received from the parents, and dare not be damaged," believing that if a person dies and allows his abdomen to be cut open and his limbs broken, he is a great sinner in Confucianism and is despised by mankind. I remember that more than ten years ago, it was reported that a doctor (whose surname is forgotten) dissected the body of his uncle, which aroused public attack and involved legal proceedings. It shows the importance that the Chinese people attach to corpses. This time, Mr. Yu's body dissection broke the public's outdated psychology and made them understand the true meaning of dissection. The significance is so great.

All human beings always hope that the doctor has an accurate diagnosis, because the outcome of the disease is closely related to the diagnosis. Therefore, the most important thing for doctors with rich knowledge and experience is to identify the type of disease, observe the changes in the condition, and then make an accurate diagnosis before determining the appropriate and rational treatment. Unfortunately, when encountering difficult to diagnose and life-threatening diseases, one doctor diagnoses it as disease A, and another doctor diagnoses it as disease B. When there are conflicting opinions, it is impossible to reach a conclusion. Without relying on corpse dissection, it is impossible to know where the disease is and what the disease is. For example, Mr. Yu suffered from stomach cancer. After understanding the dissection, I felt the precision of the new medical diagnosis. Let the public know the true face of new medicine. Mr. Yu really died with extra merit.

I, forgetting my shallowness, have said some of the above words. Perhaps it can arouse the attention of the people and jointly advocate corpse dissection. I hope even more that my colleagues in the new medical circle will embrace the same aspirations as Mr. Yu and set an example, so that the new medicine will be popularized to the great China as soon as possible. Mr. Yu, if he knows, will also smile in the ground.

Recent Preventive Medicine 196

— Yin Ge

The Difference Between Preventive Medicine and Hygiene: Preventive medicine and hygiene seem to be the same, but they are actually two different disciplines. Hygiene is the method of teaching individuals or groups to avoid disease or death. Preventive medicine refers to all possible methods of directly maintaining health. For example, avoiding sewage and bad food to avoid typhoid fever, and avoiding things that weaken the body. This belongs to hygiene. As for injecting typhoid vaccine, that belongs to the scope of preventive medicine.

Hygiene is something that we humans have been able to pay attention to since ancient times. For example, there are many precepts in religion regarding food and drink, which are actually hygienic methods. And not only humans have hygiene, but also the livestock and garden plants we see around us. For example, cattle and horses can distinguish harmful grass and do not bite it. The direction of plant growth has light avoidance, dark avoidance, humidity aversion, and dryness avoidance. These are all their hygiene rules. Therefore, personal hygiene is not unique to humans. On the contrary, preventive medicine is only available to humans. Animals do not have a positive behavior to prevent disease or physical weakness. Therefore, preventive medicine is a phenomenon unique to humans, who are called "the spirit of all things," and it is also a symbol of cultural progress.

Achievements of Preventive Medicine Practitioners: Preventive medicine also had its beginnings in ancient times. For example, primitive aborigines used antidotes to avoid the danger of poisonous arrows, or to weaken the toxicity. Aborigines also gradually increased the amount of toxins absorbed to avoid the harm of arsenic and increase the body's resistance. These can all be regarded as a method of preventive medicine.

Jenner: It was not until modern times that there was preventive inoculation against smallpox. The English Jenner discovered this method through experience. In 1798, Jenner made it practical through experimentation. This great discovery is the first glorious page in the history of preventive medicine. At that time, people could not understand the reason for vaccination and its actual benefits. It was not until a hundred years later that the world knew it. Later, Pasteur in France and others in the Jenner lineage made more discoveries. Pasteur first discovered preventive inoculation against rabies in preventive medicine. This discovery was made by Pasteur, Beylen, and Luo in 1885. The method is also very effective. Like vaccination, it is still used today without any changes. Those who suffer from the disease are all blessed by it.

The above two are good examples of preventive medicine. In recent years, the development of preventive medicine has been based on hygiene bacteriology. The prevention of infectious diseases has been increasingly successful.

Ramen: In the second and third years, the preventive injection of diphtheria was also completed. As generally known, children are prone to this disease from the age of one to six. The treatment of this disease is most effective with serum therapy. This was invented by Bering and Kitazato forty years ago. However, in recent years, Dr. Ramen, the head of the serum department of the Pasteur Institute in France, worked hard on serum production during the European War. He accidentally noticed a precious phenomenon in the test tube. After the war, he began to study it. In 1922, he discovered a new phenomenon based on the interaction between toxin and antitoxin. Soon, he used this new phenomenon as a basis and discovered the complete prevention method of diphtheria. The method he invented is to add one liter of newly filtered and highly potent diphtheria toxin to four milliliters of formaldehyde and place it in a 38-degree incubator.

Page 14

for one month. The originally powerful toxin becomes a harmless substance to the human body and can be completely immunized because it produces specific antitoxins. This substance is named diphtheria immunogen. Take a very small amount of it and inject it subcutaneously three or two times every one or two weeks, which can make us completely immune to the actual diphtheria. The immunity is effective for about five years. In this way, young children can be completely freed from the threat of diphtheria bacteria. The reduction in the incidence rate is very significant. Now all countries are eager to implement it. Italy has even issued an edict regarding this matter. In areas where diphtheria is prevalent, children aged one to five must be injected with this agent. (To be continued)

The Question of the Duration of Pregnancy... Reply to Mr. Wang Ping... 197

— Qu Shaoheng

In reply. Shaoheng previously went to Ping for business. I just returned to Shanghai yesterday. I received your esteemed letter with respect. The issue you discussed regarding the duration of pregnancy has myths in both the East and the West since ancient times. However, considering today's scientific obstetrics, it inevitably becomes a laughingstock. Nevertheless, the best basis is facts. Often, what the world deems impossible may indeed exist. It is not impossible to create a new record in obstetrics. According to this matter, there are significant differences in civil law. Therefore, most European and American countries have explicit regulations. It is a pity that our country still lacks them. The regulations of various countries listed in my book "Lectures on Obstetrics" are based on the civil laws before 1928. Whether there have been any changes since then, I have not had time to verify. Therefore, the duration of pregnancy also follows the records of famous books by medical pioneers in various countries. I dare not make any arbitrary or unfounded claims. Your friend's wife has had doubts because the duration of both pregnancies exceeded the normal range. In my opinion, this is quite valuable for research. However, the most exceptional case known to Shaoheng, as mentioned by Zongemeister, is only 355 days. However, because it is not commonly seen in various books, it was not adopted. Besides that, there is no factual record to rely on, and there is a lack of previous cases. I dare not deceive the world with frivolity. Your letter mentioned that the duration of pregnancy can exceptionally extend to fifteen or sixteen months. Shaoheng is shallow and ignorant and is willing to accept guidance. Could you please provide the book title so that I can increase my knowledge? I am deeply grateful. Respectfully replying.

Appendix: Letter from Mr. Wang 198

Great Physician Shaoheng,

I recently read your book "Lectures on Obstetrics" (1928 edition) at a friend's house. I admire it immensely. However, the section on the duration of pregnancy still does not resolve my doubts. I am specifically asking for your expert guidance. I hope you will take the trouble to answer. A friend of mine says that his wife is very virtuous. They have been married for eight years and have two children. (She reportedly still has menstruation during pregnancy.) The first child was born fifteen months after my friend left home. The second child was born twelve months after he left home. Considering the prescribed days of pregnancy, his wife must be unchaste. However, after consulting other books, the duration of pregnancy can exceptionally extend to fifteen or sixteen months. Your book does not mention this. It also says that according to British regulations, the longest is only 320 days. (The number does not match the original book. Shaoheng's note) Is there any exceptional extension of the duration of pregnancy? I hope to receive a reply. Also, has our country's civil law recently stipulated anything in this regard? Please also inform me. Respectfully wishing you good health.

Scientific Childbirth Essays (18) 199

— Yu Songyun

(10) (4) Management of Postpartum Hemorrhage

(A) Normal Bleeding and Abnormal Bleeding

Normal bleeding occurs twice, once before and once after delivery. The first time is when labor is imminent. The mucus discharged is mixed with thin blood. The second time is after the expulsion of the afterbirth, due to the separation of the placenta, there is slightly more bleeding. This kind of bleeding naturally stops after the placenta and membranes are completely separated, because the broken blood vessel openings are sealed by the contraction force of the uterus. Otherwise, if the uterine contraction is poor, and the broken openings cannot be completely closed, bleeding will continue, leading to life-threatening danger.

In short, the amount of bleeding during normal delivery varies from woman to woman, but at least 200 grams to at most 600 grams. If it exceeds this amount, it is abnormal bleeding.

(B) Causes of Abnormal Bleeding

The main symptom of placenta previa is bleeding. Placenta previa can be marginal, lateral, or central. Bleeding due to placenta previa generally occurs suddenly without external inducement. The timing of occurrence can be determined by the location of the placenta attachment. Marginal bleeding is the latest, mostly at the beginning of the tenth month of pregnancy. The second is lateral, bleeding occurs earlier, around the ninth month of pregnancy. Central bleeding is the earliest, mostly occurring in the seventh month of pregnancy.

Bleeding from placenta previa can be small or large, varying in amount. It may be a large amount at the initial occurrence, or it may be small at first and then increase, eventually leading to anemia, or even death.

Abnormal bleeding is also the main sign of premature placental abruption. Why does premature placental abruption occur? It is mostly due to the mother suffering from endometritis, or pregnancy-induced nephritis, strenuous physical activity, abdominal contusions, tough membranes, or membranes that are not easily ruptured, leading to internal and external bleeding. The internally shed blood accumulates between the uterine wall and the detached placenta and membranes. The bleeding is not seen externally. If the blood flows out externally, the symptoms are no different from internal bleeding. After internal and external bleeding occurs, the lower abdomen suddenly experiences severe pain, the uterus enlarges and becomes very tense, labor pains stop, the pulse becomes rapid and weak, breathing becomes difficult, the limbs become cold, consciousness becomes blurred, the face becomes pale, cold sweat breaks out, the vision becomes blurred, and the ears ring, or even leading to acute anemia and death.

(C) Treatment of Abnormal Bleeding

After abnormal bleeding is discovered, a doctor should be consulted immediately for treatment. However, as an emergency measure, an ice pack can be placed on the lower abdomen. The patient should lie down with her head low and legs high. Bleeding wounds are most susceptible to mold invasion. Before the doctor sutures the wound, special attention should be paid to cleanliness.

If the bleeding from placenta previa is mild, rest quietly. If the bleeding is severe, perform vaginal tamponade, artificial rupture of membranes, foot breech extraction, uterine dilation, and other procedures. When there is high-grade bleeding in premature placental abruption, removal of the uterine contents is the best strategy. When necessary, vaginal dilation, vaginal tamponade, amniocentesis, and one of the procedures such as forceps craniotomy and fetal reduction should be performed. If a hematoma occurs in the vagina, a cloth soaked in 1% Lysol can be used to apply pressure. If it has ruptured, use a compression bandage.

Talks on Heliotherapy 200

— Ding Huikang

Heliotherapy is the method of using sunlight to improve human health or treat diseases. Its effectiveness is mostly due to the ultraviolet rays contained in sunlight. Therefore, heliotherapy must be carried out under sunlight with sufficient ultraviolet rays to be legitimate. However, the ultraviolet rays emitted from sunlight are easily absorbed by coal smoke, dust, and water vapor in the air. At the same time, they can also be absorbed by the air. Therefore, sunbathing is most effective far away from cities, in high altitudes with thin air. However, on the plains, wherever there is direct sunlight, sunbathing will have considerable effects.

Effects

Sunbathing is effective for all weak constitutions and all chronic diseases. It is especially effective for chronic tuberculous diseases, such as tuberculosis, pleura, peritoneal tuberculosis, kidney, bladder, genital tuberculosis, bone and joint tuberculosis, skin tuberculosis, and so on.

Generally, for tuberculous diseases, quiet therapy is adopted. For example, for tuberculosis, the patient is made to lie down quietly. For joint tuberculosis, plaster bandages are used to fix the affected area so that it can be fully quiet. The goal is to use the body's inherent resistance to resist pathogens and parasites and to use the immunity generated by the body's natural reactions to wait for the recovery of the diseased body.

Heliotherapy is a more proactive method. Sunlight is directly shone on the skin and affected area (when there are wounds) of the whole body to stimulate the body, increase its resistance, and promote the occurrence of immunity. If the body is too weak, there may be danger when sunbathing. It should be carried out under the guidance of a doctor.

Method

For heliotherapy, "first," the entire spectrum of sunlight must be used. If it is in a glass shed, the outer line is absorbed by the glass, which is ineffective. It must be performed directly under sunlight. "Second," heliotherapy must be gradual. Do not rush it to avoid failure. On the first day, only expose the feet (from heel to toe) for five minutes. On the second day, expose the lower legs (from knee to heel) for five minutes, and expose the feet for ten minutes. On the third day, expose the upper legs for five minutes, expose the lower legs for ten minutes, and expose the feet for fifteen minutes. In this way, the area exposed to direct sunlight is gradually expanded and the time is increased daily, until it reaches the entire body. "Third," sunbathing must be in direct contact with sunlight. Wearing clothes towards the sun cannot be called sunbathing. After sunbathing, the spirit is extremely refreshed, just like the pleasure gained after exercise. If appetite increases, one can sleep soundly and resistance is increased. The affected area also tends to heal more easily. The effectiveness is indeed not insignificant.

Free Discussion

Writing Books and Teaching 201

— Guo Dafu

Writers and teachers both walk the same path concerning books, but these two professions are absolutely incompatible. This is a fact that those who have not personally experienced it cannot understand. People generally think that teaching can lead to writing a book using the teaching materials. And a writer, before finishing his book, can use the collected materials to teach. These two things are one and two, two and one, the easiest and simplest things. But little do they know that the joys and hardships involved are far beyond what ordinary people can imagine.

First, let's talk about the purpose of writing and teaching. The main purpose of both is, of course, the same: to spread knowledge and create culture. Secondly, the secondary purpose is, of course, something that no one can avoid: to make a living. That's right, the purpose of writers and teachers is exactly the same. But if people think that these two things are one and the same just because their purposes are the same, then they are wrong. Because the processes involved in achieving these purposes are very different.

First, there is a big difference between the audience or listeners (The Audience) and the readers (The Reading Public). The readership of a writer has no restrictions on time, place, age, knowledge, class, occupation, etc., while the audience of a teacher is generally subject to the various restrictions mentioned above. Also, the readership of a writer rarely meets the writer, while the audience of a teacher is facing living and breathing people. Just from this point alone, we can feel how free the writer is and how much the teacher is bound! Therefore, many people with good knowledge often cannot speak when they stand on the podium; while many people with strong eloquence can speak fluently even without real knowledge, making listeners admire them.

Second, there is the psychological change between the writer and the teacher: Because the writer enjoys the many freedoms mentioned above, his entire mind can focus on the writing itself. He doesn't mind being meticulous, he's not afraid of being profound, he polishes and refines his work until he feels satisfied, and then he publishes it. And the teacher, because the person sitting there listening attentively is a feeling-filled animal called a "human," he has no choice but to be dominated by the feelings of the audience, depending on the time and place. Once emotions move, the line of thought will be scattered. Not to mention the speaker's own emotions, just the reaction caused by the audience's emotions reflecting into the speaker's heart is enough to make it difficult for the teacher to have complete confidence. What's more, modern youths are rebellious creatures!

Third, there is the conflict between reason and emotion. Those who engage in creative literature (Creative Literature) or creation should absolutely not teach; because creators must be based on emotion, while teachers emphasize reason. The extension and cultivation of reason can often kill emotion, and the emotional heat wave can also easily disrupt reason. Therefore, a great poet may become the worst professor of poetry when asked to teach poetry. The reading of a poet is sometimes far inferior to the rehearsal (Rehearsal) of a third-rate actor. However, China has a bad habit of often inviting creators to teach or lecture. This is a thing that has a hundred harms and no benefits. It is a minor matter if the audience is disappointed for a moment and regrets being deceived. But if the creator loses his inspiration and poetry forever due to temporary constraints, that is a great loss to the nation! May 20, 1933

Interrupted Reunion 202

— Jinming

The soft green of Beihai Park spread among all the branches and leaves in a gentle and warm breeze. Boats were rocking back and forth on the waves, along with old and new aquatic plants, cormorants and wild ducks.

I often go alone to that secluded corner to find a seat because I am looking for a little "quiet". At the north end of the park, there are three glass pavilions connected together, facing the water and backing onto a series of earthen rocks. Among the chaotic tourists, one can still find the nature that is not submerged.

In the afternoon, the park is like the stock market's opening. Those who come to the park in the morning must be lonely people left over from the world, or those who come to seek some relief. Touring during the opening seems to have other functions. People seem to think that way.

Sitting in that glass pavilion - the one facing east - it has been half an hour; the Longjing tea is not genuine, but it is light enough. I have to use strong cigarettes to stimulate myself. People who live in big cities and lead lives full of intense stimuli crave things that are as light as water. But when they try it, they feel some regret. My vision scatters into the gaps, but it is soon reined in by the questions called out in my mind. Only the air is fresh, making my lungs feel refreshed.

"Hey, hurry up! Add three seats."

This abrupt voice made me turn my head to look at a patron behind me - young but showing signs of aging, trying hard to decorate himself luxuriously on an unsuitable body - with an agitated face. His companion, someone who looked like him, stood waiting for something.

Their guests were two women and a boy in a gown about sixteen or seventeen years old. They bowed to the host with unusual restraint. They were all slender and plump, with dull expressions. Naturally, they were already at the end of "Youth Bridge". The lost joy had left a sad shadow on their pale faces.

They sat down around the tea table. It seemed that everyone knew everyone else. Each person was measuring the emotions brought about by this moment. Then came humility and polite greetings. And the opening words were nothing more than admiration, coming from an attitude that did not necessarily have to be sincere.

"Ms. R… Your English at N University, everyone knows that you are the best…"

The host, the young man in the green woolen coat, said in his speech.

There was not much sincere reaction; the taller one only smiled modestly.

"You're too kind."

Humility is naturally a way to express status and "style", and in front of the public, they are talking about things they don't want to talk about, and smiling smiles they don't want to smile. Precisely because between men and women, the eyes of others are sharp and unkind.

The young man in the green woolen coat steered the conversation back.

"Do you know Mr. Song, Ms. R…?"

"Maybe, I don't remember clearly."

The speaker raised her teacup and looked at her partner. Perhaps as a result of being overly cautious, she felt that the other party's casual tone contained ulterior motives. So she was perplexed - a little perplexed - and sought to correct herself.

The boy who came with the two ladies was quiet, looking out the window, like a supervisor who didn't care about anything, never opening his mouth.

"He is Tong Youxin, the director of studies at Huazhong Middle School."

"Ah!" the woman said, "It seems I don't know him very well."

The host's companion, the young man in the hemp coat, seemed to be lowering his head and faking a smile because his face was too dark. There seemed to be a strange and disgusting emotion pressing in his throat.

"Youxin, he also knows that Ms. R's English is very, very good. He often expresses his admiration to others!"

The host was still saying such meaningless things.

The woman was just being polite as usual. Her companion, who seemed to be her sister, had a mocking smile, glancing at the young man in the hemp coat from time to time.

"At the same time, I feel something about Tong… He thinks… because the school needs teachers, so he expressed his interest to me…"

"Oh, is that so?" the woman said.

"He is wondering if Ms. R can teach some classes there?"

The woman's words softened a bit, saying:

"Don't be so polite. You're really too kind."

The people at the table felt uncomfortable. They murmured among themselves; they paid close attention to the changes in psychology in their conversation…

"Teaching is naturally not a matter of being polite…"

The host said this way.

The younger of the two women spoke some dialect to the boy who came with her. The boy stood up immediately and expressed his intention to the host - to leave. It seemed that whether they were asked to stay or not, a cup of tea and a few polite words were already very thin gestures of friendship… so he left his seat and rejected all inducements to talk.

They bowed deeply to the two young men, and with their eyes looking straight ahead, they left with style - this was naturally the result of decades of education - or walked away gracefully.

The people at the table were dissatisfied and unhappy, because they sensed that these two young men would fail to be selected. They are not beautiful, and they are too restrained. What's the use of talking about civilized things?

The two young men, however, were highly skilled at concealing their feelings - naturally, those who are used to concealing their feelings cannot obtain extraordinary experiences - and said this:

"If we had known that they wouldn't teach, why did we invite them?"

"I thought so too."

"I think we should still look for Li Renwu."

"Naturally."

And so they left, handsome and carefree!

February 1, 1933, in Beiping. On the way back from a visit to Beihai

Ramblings from Qulu 203

— Zizhan

(32) Evidence from a Poem

In my previous discussion of the Tang Caichang case, I cited Zhang Taiyan's article "The Morality of Revolution" as evidence, saying that Long Zehou "led Wen Tingshi to Wuchang to start the affair." Soon after, I received a letter from Mr. Wen Gongzhi, refuting the accusation against his esteemed father. His words were very credible, roughly saying, "After my late father retired from office, he traveled between Shanghai and Guangdong. He went to Japan because he was implicated in the reform movement. He did not return until 1901. How could he have gone to Hubei? My late father was the initiator of the Society for National Strengthening. The society was seized by Kang Youwei. He suffered from world-weariness and resentment and died in sorrow. If he had informed, he should have received a great reward. How could he have ended up like this? Moreover, after Lord Tang died, his younger brother Caizhong was still alive and could have been consulted." Recently, reading Yunqixuan's collection of poems has further confirmed that the distinguished Mr. Wen did not inform. I will only cite his poem "Southern Village Tune" as evidence. This was Mr. Wen's lighthearted work during his later years of illness. The poem says:

A room sick like Vimalakirti, glad to see the idle courtyard closed to birds. Cooking medicine and turning books are full of flavor; ha ha, I, an old man, have no worries about what the world will do! Vast old mountains and rivers, who sheds more tears toward the New Pavilion? Only the partridge's song can say, "Brother! What can be done when the time is not right?"

It can be seen that Mr. Wen had unfulfilled ambitions and died in sorrow. He claimed to have no worries, but in fact he was always concerned about the state and the country. Because Mr. Gongzhi wrote to me asking for a correction, I specifically clarify it here.

Carrot Top 204

— Jules Renard, translated by Lin Quzuo

Fountain Pen (Continued)

Lepic: And German?

Carrot Top: German pronunciation is extremely difficult, Dad.

Lepic: Beast! What, if war is declared with Germany, you won't even understand their writing? How will you deal with those Prussians?

Carrot Top: Ah! By the time war is declared, I'll have plenty of time to learn. You always use war to scare me. But I think it will definitely wait until after I graduate to break out.

Lepic: What was your last essay score? I hope you're not at the bottom of the list.

Carrot Top: But someone has to be at the bottom of the list.

Lepic: Beast! I really want to take you out to dinner. If today were still Sunday! But during the school term, I absolutely do not want to disturb your studies.

Carrot Top: I personally don't have any important homework; how about you, Felix?

Felix: Exactly, this morning the teacher forgot to give us practice problems.

Lepic: But you can go and study the book a little more.

Felix: Ah! I've already memorized it, Dad. That's the lesson from yesterday.

Lepic: But in any case, I still want you to go back to school. I'll find a way to wait until Sunday, and then we can all go out to dinner together.

The time for farewell had come. Whether the older brother Felix looked disgruntled or Carrot Top pretended to be silent, they finally couldn't avoid parting.

Carrot Top waited for this moment of departure with anxiety.

"I wonder if my score will be better this time," he thought in his heart, "and whether my father is actually unhappy about my hugging and kissing him."

He made up his mind, looked straight ahead, raised his mouth high, and walked closer.

But Lepic stopped him with one hand and kept him at a distance, saying:

"That fountain pen on your ear is going to blind me. When you hug and kiss me, can't you put your pen somewhere else? Please pay attention to the fact that I've already taken off my cigarette?"

Carrot Top: Ah! Good Dad, please forgive me. Really, one day something unfortunate will happen because of my mistakes. Others have warned me long ago, but my pen fits so well on my ear that I've been keeping it there, and I've forgotten about it myself. I should have at least taken off the pen tip! Ah! Good Dad, it really makes me happy that I know my pen scares you.

Lepic: Beast! You almost blinded me, and you're happy about it?

Carrot Top: No, Good Dad, I'm happy about something else: I'm happy about a stupid idea in my mind.

Red Cheeks

The dean of St. Mark's College, as usual, checked the dormitory for a week and then left. Every student rolled into bed, as if hidden in a tube, shrunk small to avoid fogging out of bed. Supervisor Mr. Weiaolong looked around with his head held high, and seeing that everyone had fallen asleep, he stood on tiptoe and slowly twisted down the gas lamp. Suddenly, the students sleeping on the beds began to talk softly to their neighbors. The whispers between beds grew louder and louder. These moving lips caused a mixed sound throughout the dormitory. Sometimes, a short whistle or two would seep into the mixed sound. (To be continued)

Jinghai Zhuan Kan, Issue 23, Published every Sunday

Several Paths to Reviving Chinese Tea 205

— Yi'an

I. The Tragic Decline of Foreign Sales

China is not only the motherland of tea production, but decades ago, all the tea consumed in the world was supplied by China. In China's foreign trade, tea exports accounted for more than 50% of the total at their peak. In the remote and impoverished areas of Hunan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, Fujian, and Zhejiang provinces, hundreds of thousands or even millions of households relied on tea production income to support their rural economies.

Since the successive development of Indian, Ceylon, and Javanese black tea, China's black tea exports have declined year by year, from a maximum of more than 1.66 million dan (in 1880) to just over 100,000 dan. Black tea from Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, and Wenzhou in Zhejiang Province has almost no foothold in domestic and foreign markets, except for Qimen black tea from Anhui and its neighboring areas, which still have considerable characteristics in terms of quality and can barely serve as a decoration.

Green tea, on the one hand, accounts for only one-eighth of the demand for black tea in various countries, and its foreign sales are not as high as those of black tea. On the other hand, it is also subject to competition from Japanese tea. Sales in the United States have been declining year by year, and sales in Africa are also gradually becoming dangerous. In recent years, the high-quality Chun Mee green tea produced in Wuyuan, Shexian, and Xiuning in Anhui, and the Pingshui tea produced in Shaoxing, Shangyu, and Shengxian in Zhejiang, are also in a precarious state!

Oolong tea produced in Fujian was originally one of the important products for export, but now it is also subject to competition from Taiwanese tea. Not only has the quantity decreased, but it will even disappear from overseas markets!

II. The Biggest Weakness

Although China is the motherland of tea, it is just like China being an old and large nation. The technology of cultivation and manufacturing is inferior to others, and the methods of sales promotion are inferior to others. No matter how excellent the natural quality is, it cannot be spared from being damaged and eliminated by others.

Why is China's tea industry so severely damaged? This is a question that those who care about the tea industry, or those who understand China's politics, economy, society, and culture, can give detailed reasons for, and there is no need to elaborate here. Now, let's briefly mention a few more fundamental issues.

(1) Aging Tea Trees: Tea tree cultivation in China mostly belongs to farmers' sideline occupations. They are casually propagated next to houses and on mountainsides. Modern cultivation techniques such as fertilization and pruning are certainly lacking, and even the necessary weeding and cultivation depend on the price of tea. In the past, when exports were strong and profits were high, not only could people pay attention to weeding and cultivation, but also new tea fields could be expanded or replanted from time to time. Now, except for casually picking some tender and old leaves in the spring for personal use or because it is required to be sent to the landlord as a tribute, they are sold if they can be sold; otherwise, they will no longer pay much attention to this unprofitable business. As a result, the remaining tea plants that have survived for hundreds of years or decades will inevitably gradually age. The more the tree weakens, the harder the tea becomes, and the lower the quality becomes. This point is not only not valued by ordinary tea merchants, but also most people who talk about tea industry issues have not paid attention to it. Let's take an example. Sichuan tea is inferior to that of Hubei and Hunan, Hubei and Hunan tea is inferior to that of Ningzhou, and Ningzhou tea is inferior to that of Qimen. This is a clear example, because Sichuan is the birthplace of China's tea industry, and it gradually developed from the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, while the development of Qimen is still a matter of the last thirty to fifty years.

(2) Inferior Manufacturing: China has the most tea manufacturing methods. Since the history of tea, it cannot be said that the manufacturing methods are not sophisticated. As early as 1140 or 1150 years ago, the "Classic of Tea" written by Lu Yu of the Tang Dynasty recorded the drinking methods in great detail, but compared with the modern mechanization and scientification in India and Japan, it is naturally inferior! Simply put, the only requirement for green tea is to have a clear and fragrant color and taste, and the important standard for black tea is to have a bright color and a lasting tea taste. The former requires clear water color, and the latter requires clean vinegar fermentation. The scientific manufacturing method is not complicated. It is about how to use the two pigments chlorophyll and carotenoid, as well as the acid-degrading enzymes, contained in each kind of fresh tea leaves. When making green tea, high temperature is used to stop the action of carotenoid and melting enzymes that will turn red, so that not only the color of the green tea leaves is clear and the fragrance is increased, but also it will never change color. When making black tea, the opposite is true. An appropriate temperature is used to make the acidizing enzymes gradually change naturally until the original green leaves turn bright red. This is so scientific, and the taste, aroma, and even the shape are the same. The reason why the water color of Chinese red and green tea is not clear and the taste is not very lasting is that the manufacturing methods cannot be fully utilized. As a result, more than seven-tenths of the exported green tea must be artificially colored with various colors to deceive people. Black tea vinegar fermentation only uses sunlight and cannot adjust the temperature indoors, so it is subject to natural control and cannot compete with Indian and Ceylon tea!

(3) Too Many Names: Chinese people and domestic tea merchants often boast to the world about the breadth of our country's tea-producing areas and the variety of types. Of course, no one can match us in this regard, but precisely because of this, there are different manufacturing methods in different places; different shapes, colors, and luster; different tastes and aromas; thus, various different names are produced. Either named after the place, or named after the time, or named after the shape, or named after the object. If you add up the statistics, there are countless thousands of types. Speaking specifically of exported tea: Although the total number of names is only about twenty, there are great differences in the thickness and grades of the same type. In this way, not only is it extremely difficult to promote to foreign countries, but even foreign merchants cannot use a unified name and a unified price for unified sales. India's Lipton tea only has three grades of tea: yellow label, red label, and peach red label, and three prices, which are naturally conducive to promotion and sales.

(4) Excessive Exploitation: The Chinese people have suffered from thousands of years of feudal exploitation, especially in rural areas, where the exploitation is so heavy that there is no need to elaborate. In the past, during the prosperous era of tea trade, it didn't matter if they were heavily exploited. Now, costs are rising, tea prices are falling, local taxes and levies, merchant deductions, and foreign merchant monopolies are even worse than before. Qimen tea, known as the king of Chinese black tea, although the market price of new tea these days is lower than in previous years, it still goes up to 200 yuan per dan, but the price at which inland tea farmers sell to tea firms is only 5 jiao per jin using a 22-liang scale. Although it is too wet and must be dried to make less than half the weight, they can get at most only half the original price. Although this half of the amount still has to include the cost of packaging, manufacturing, and transportation, most of it is spent in the heavy exploitation relationship. Therefore, since the eighth year of the Republic of China, although export taxes have always been exempted, the sluggishness of tea exports remains the same. This does not mean that the government's restoration of export taxes is supported, but it is only to illustrate that other exploitation relationships are too serious, and simply exempting export taxes has no greater impact on the facts.

(5) Lack of Organization: The poor cultivation and manufacturing methods naturally make it difficult to compete with various countries. Too many names and excessive exploitation are certainly the biggest shortcomings in terms of promotion and cost, but the lack of a proper organization is also one of the major reasons why China's tea industry cannot be improved. Although there are strict organizations such as inland tea merchants, especially introduction houses in Shanghai and Hankou, they only protect the merchants' own groups, and although there are enthusiastic people, they are only a very small number. Just look at the tea industry improvement committees in India and Ceylon, which have various organizations for research, improvement, promotion, and publicity. Just the expenses from the tea surcharge income collected by the Advertising Propaganda Bureau (The Ceylon Mca Propaganda Board) organized in Ceylon last June reach more than 2.5 million yuan per year. The Japanese tea industry association has practical unions in counties and the central government, with clear systems for internal and external affairs. The expenses spent on the tea industry each year are also around one million yuan. These are all things that we cannot hope to achieve. There are certainly countless other shortcomings. Now, let's move on to discussing several paths to improve Chinese tea.

III. Revival Methods

It is not difficult to improve production techniques and eliminate exploitation relationships. Although the improvement of technology should theoretically go through a considerable period of research; but as far as the tea industry is concerned, on the one hand, it is not necessary to go through variety improvement like rice, wheat, and other crops, which often takes several years. It is enough to choose a site and engage in cultivation and active manufacturing at the same time. Secondly, India's black tea manufacturing and Japan's green tea manufacturing have already achieved considerable results. According to the results of this year's trials in various places, it can be said that 70 to 80% of the success has been achieved, and the goal can be achieved by imitating them. As for the point of exploitation, as long as politics is slightly on track, a piece of order, a few laws, can achieve considerable results in the shortest period of time. Therefore, reviving China's tea industry is no longer a question of how to improve production and eliminate exploitation relationships; but a question of what method to use to proceed; simply put, it is about how we should "do" it!

Our ways of doing it roughly fall into these three categories:

The first is the capitalist method. This is to imitate the way the British did it in India and Ceylon. Choose suitable tea-producing areas, use a large number of machines and a large area of tea planting to produce the necessary quantity for foreign promotion, from tens of thousands of dan to hundreds of thousands of dan to millions of dan. If it goes smoothly, it can be a small success in ten years and a great success in twenty years. However, the world's capitalism is now approaching its end. Regardless of whether China has such a large capital force, not to mention that China's tea production method is a small-farmer sideline type and has seasonality, with a maximum of only three or four productions per year, unlike the tropical areas of India and Ceylon, where it can be picked and manufactured all year round; not to mention that they already have decades of deep-rooted power, and the emerging small capitalism is difficult to compete with them. Therefore, this capitalist road is not easy to take.

The second is the cooperative type, which can also be said to be the road that Japan is currently taking. In the shortest possible time, we will formulate tea industry cooperation regulations and order all tea-producing provinces and counties, whether they are cultivators or manufacturers, to join the cooperative, and provide them with cash advances using new methods to enable them to jointly produce, jointly manufacture, and jointly sell; there is also a cooperative federation, which is preparing for joint direct export. This is certainly the most ideal and appropriate method. However, its shortcoming is that it is slow. Especially in China, where the territory is large, there are few talents, and farmers are too impatient to cooperate, it is inevitable that one thing is fixed only for something else to break, and besides, the countryside has frequently gone bankrupt, and the tea industry is so declining, how can we have the patience to slowly improve it? Therefore, this path is possible, but it cannot be taken at once!

The third is the state-owned type, which is also the unified way. Now, to revive China's rural areas, we must use revolutionary methods. The same is true for rural farmers and the tea industry. This so-called state-owned method should use the power of the central and provincial governments and the people to jointly operate, select suitable tea-producing areas in various provinces, delimit tea areas, and use the latest scientific methods to dispatch specialized personnel to cultivate and manufacture separately. All matters related to cultivation, manufacturing, and sales are carried out according to national plans. It is planned for six tea-producing provinces: (1) Hunan Province selects Anhua, Taoyuan, Pingjiang, and Xiangtan counties, producing 100,000 dan of black tea per year; (2) Hubei Province selects Puchi and Chongyang counties, producing 100,000 dan of black tea; (3) Jiangxi Province selects the vicinity of the former Ningzhou, producing 100,000 dan of black tea; (4) Anhui Province produces 100,000 dan of black tea in Qimen, Zhizhi (i.e., Qiupu), and Fuliang in Jiangxi, and 100,000 dan of Chun Mee in Wuyuan, Shexian, and Xiuning; (5) Zhejiang Province produces 100,000 dan of Pingshui green tea in the old Shaoxing counties, 50,000 dan of green tea in the Huzhou area, and 50,000 dan of black tea in Wenzhou; (6) Fujian Province produces 100,000 dan of green tea in the northern counties of Fuan and Fuding, and 100,000 dan of black tea in the western counties of Chong'an and Jian'an. This is a rough calculation, with an annual output of about 900,000 dan. With these 900,000 dan of improved red and green tea leaves, we can fight head-on with various tea-producing countries. Not only will the weak Japanese green tea fall at the first blow, but even Indian and Ceylon black tea will have to retreat. However, this unified method certainly has its advantages in terms of technological improvement, production consistency, and publicity and promotion, but the current government and people do not have such spiritual strength. As for state-owned, how easy is it to talk about? So, what should our current route be? Let's make a conclusion as follows.

The capitalist method should not be taken, the cooperative method is difficult to implement for a while, and the state-owned method that is in line with modern times cannot be taken now, so we have to take a mixed route of the second and third methods. This mixed route is that after the central and provincial governments have delimited the tea-producing areas in the country, on the one hand, they organize tea farmers, and on the other hand, they assign personnel to be responsible for guidance. From near to far, from small to large, we will conduct pilot projects in the first two to three years, and we can achieve small success in eight to ten years. But in any case, the most urgent things at present are, first, to thoroughly investigate the actual situation of tea-producing areas in the country; second, to quickly cultivate talents to guide the tea industry; and third, to first organize a group of competent authorities and tea merchants in the tea-producing provinces to discuss all the implementation plans.

Japanese Tea Industry and Its Aggression War Against China 206

— Juenong

Japan originally had no tea trees. It was only in 805 AD that tea was introduced to the country from China. In 1191, the second year of Shaoxi of Emperor Guangzong of the Song Dynasty, a large number of tea seeds were imported and propagated in various places. At first, they did not know how to manufacture tea, and they hired Chinese technicians to guide them; even for foreign exports, they had to entrust Chinese merchants to handle it in the beginning.

Since 1870, Japan began to carry out a tea industry innovation movement, sending personnel to China, India and other places for on-site investigation and research, and importing Indian tea-making machinery to first engage in the manufacture of black tea, and then gradually expanding the machinery for green tea to reduce manufacturing costs. Among them, the most alarming to us is the progress in methods such as pruning and fertilization, which not only improved the quality of the tea itself, but also greatly increased the yield per mu.

Year | Average Tea Garden Area (Mu) | Index | Average Tea Production (Dan) | Index

------- | -------- | -------- | -------- | --------

1892-1896 | 944,842 | 120 | 498,926 | 95

1897-1901 | 851,191 | 107 | 471,707 | 91

1902-1906 | 807,758 | 102 | 433,512 | 84

1907-1911 | 794,588 | 100 | 517,562 | 100

1912-1916 | 784,196 | 99 | 570,062 | 111

1917-1921 | 781,870 | 98 | 628,837 | 121

1922-1926 | 712,904 | 90 | 604,437 | 117

1927-1931 | 663,225 | 84 | 641,250 | 124

From the above table, we can see that although the area of tea gardens has decreased regularly year by year; the amount of tea produced in the past 30 years has increased very regularly. The progress of cultivation technology is the most noteworthy fact.

The driving force behind the progress of the Japanese tea industry is twofold. On the one hand, of course, is the government's advocacy and encouragement; and on the other hand, it is the organized and systematic tea industry association. This tea industry association is not like the guilds or associations gathered by merchants who only covet a portion of the benefits in China, but a group that unites tea farmers, sellers, tea shops, tea warehouses, and even exporters to seek the common interests of the tea industry. From villages to cities and counties to the central government, there is a systematic and very clear organization, which is similar to the cooperative organization currently advocated in China. Internally, it provides guidance and improvement, and externally, it promotes publicity. The government plans and subsidizes it, and the association makes active activities in all directions.

Now let's talk about foreign activities, which are actually the facts of fighting against Chinese tea. Because Japan only produces green tea, and the foreign sales of green tea, in the past and even now, are only to China.

Japan's foreign trade previously only included the United States and Canada, and the quantity to Canada was not very large. The sales in the United States can be said to have been completely monopolized by Chinese tea 50 or 60 years ago; but Japan used various publicity methods to gradually seize the position of Chinese tea. But the competition in the United States is already a past event; what makes us most saddened is the invasion of the largest sales markets in Russia and Africa in our country in recent years. Because in the past ten years, the only customer for Japanese green tea, the United States, has seen a year-by-year reduction due to the large-scale import of Indian, Ceylon, and Javanese black tea, as well as the massive dumping of coffee from South America. But the Japanese's foreign commercial policy is just like their military and diplomatic means, fierce, vicious, and invasive, and they do not choose the fat to bite, but instead take advantage of the weakness to attack. Naturally, the biggest impact is on China!

China's largest black tea sales market in the past was the United Kingdom, which had long been occupied by India and Ceylon. The secondary green tea sales market in the United States, as mentioned above, has also been taken over by Japan. Therefore, before the European War, most of it relied on Russia, and after the European War, most of it was in Africa. The Japanese painstakingly tried to please Russian merchants by taking advantage of the interruption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia; they adopted the policy of cheap dumping, spent huge amounts of advertising, and sought a way out in Africa. What was the result? They succeeded, and China's green tea exports were greatly affected! For clarity, the recent country-by-country foreign sales of Japanese tea and their figures are recorded below (unit: thousand pounds):

Country | United States | Canada | Russia | France and Morocco | China | Other

------- | -------- | -------- | -------- | -------- | -------- | --------

1928 | 19,915 | 2,538 | 1,433 | 丨丨 | 丨 | 丨

1929 | 16,969 | 2,561 | 3,312 | 丨丨 | 丨 | 11

1930 | 16,204 | 1,900 | 4,426 | 13 | 丨 | 丨

1931 | 18,590 | 1,949 | 4,862 | 555 | 414 | 2

1932 | 16,569 | 2,022 | 4,275 | 1,736 | 923 | 415

In the shortest period of time, the figures for sales to Russia and Africa have really made leaps and bounds. Sales to Russia were almost non-existent before 1926; now it accounts for the second largest tea exporting country in Japan; and in 1929, no tea was exported to Africa, but last year it reached a huge amount of more than 1.7 million pounds; what is even more heartbreaking is that the figure for tea exported to China is also about to reach a huge amount of one million pounds, and it goes without saying that this figure is for tea imported to the three northeastern provinces.

China's silk industry has almost been wiped out by Japanese silk; black tea has long been eroded by Indian and Ceylon tea and cannot recover. Now, the surviving green tea, the largest sales markets in Russia and Africa, has been occupied by Japanese tea. If we continue to be indolent and do not rise up to resist, we will inevitably follow in the footsteps of raw silk and black tea, and there will be no way to recover!

Several Examples of Tea Industry Innovation (Ying) 207

We have heard a lot about the need to improve Chinese tea manufacturing methods and to reform farmers' production and sales organizations; but how to improve? No one is doing it, and no one can show us the results! Now, giving us is also giving the community very good news, that is, improving production and improving organization are not only dawning, but also have actual results. It is written here for the common enjoyment of the people of the country.

Hunan Produces Excellent Machine-Made Green Tea 208

The Hunan Provincial Government has established a tea experiment station in Anhua, and this year it used machinery to produce semi-mechanized improved green tea. It is said that the color, aroma, and taste are all excellent, and it is much better than Japanese green tea. Hunan is a famous tea-producing area, and the labor costs are extremely low. It was thought that it would not be possible to re-manufacture green tea before, but now it has been successful. The future direction is how to promote it to the people.

Ningzhou Black Tea Has Achieved Extraordinary Results 209

The White Eagle Pit area of Ningzhou originally had a privately organized large-scale tea planting and manufacturing factory, which cost about 200,000 yuan of capital, but because of poor management, it was leased this year to the tea industry improvement farm jointly established by the Central Agricultural Experiment Institute and the Shanghai Hankou Commodity Inspection Bureau. The tea samples recently sent to Shanghai, its first-class imitation improved black tea color and taste can be comparable to Indian and Ceylon tea. Good Indian tea is currently worth about four yuan per pound on the Shanghai market. The second and third grades are also similar to the best Qimen black tea. The top price of Qihong last year was 220 taels, while Ninghong was only 70 taels, with a ratio of one to three. The farm is still in the first phase of the experiment in the shortest period of time, and it has already made a splash, giving a great stimulus to the improvement of China's tea industry!

Qimen Tea Begins to Organize a Marketing Cooperative 210

Qimen tea is now the king of Chinese black tea. Because of the inconvenience of transportation, the difference between mountain prices and market prices is always more than double. The Construction Department of the Anhui Provincial Government established a provincial tea industry improvement farm at the former site of the National Tea Industry Experiment Station. This year, in addition to preparing various new-style machines to actively seek to improve the manufacturing methods of red and green tea, it also organized a marketing cooperative for farmers. The first batch of tea has arrived in Shanghai and should be estimated at a good price in the near future. This not only opens the prelude to cooperative marketing of tea, but in the future, if it can be promoted, the production of tea can be improved, and the suffering of farmers can also be completely alleviated.

Isn't this the most noteworthy thing to report in the voice of reviving the Chinese tea industry?

Prospects for Reforming China's Tea Industry 211

— Wang Zhenhuan

Tea leaves, all grown on trees, are broadly categorized into black tea and green tea based on differing manufacturing methods. Green tea manufacturing involves two methods: pan-firing, called "chaoqing," and oven-drying, called "hongqing." In terms of color, aroma, and taste, Chinese tea is superior to tea from India, Ceylon, and Japan. However, in the early days of underdeveloped maritime transport, Chinese tea often took months, even years, to reach foreign countries. During this long journey, the color of the tea inevitably changed, affecting sales. Therefore, tea merchants artificially colored export tea, resulting in a difference between tea for foreign markets and tea for domestic consumption. Tea merchants believed that colored Chinese tea initially had good sales, but in reality, the consumers of this colored tea were not the civilized people of Europe and America, but foreign tea merchants who resold it to colored people in their colonies for profit. Europeans and Americans generally disliked drinking colored Chinese tea because they considered it detrimental to health. As a result, China's green tea trade has been declining day by day. The root cause lies entirely in the coloring process.

Therefore, improving green tea exports is not difficult; it simply requires banning coloring and adopting new manufacturing methods. Tea merchants are well aware of this, but they believe that although the colored green tea trade is declining, it can still survive. If coloring is suddenly eliminated, they fear losing even the existing sales. However, this argument is misleading. Today's maritime transport is much more advanced than before, reducing the travel time for exported green tea. Moreover, there are new green tea manufacturing methods that can keep the tea's color unchanged. Recently, the tea research stations in Hunan, Jiangxi, and Anhui provinces have achieved considerable success after conducting trials under guidance from the provincial authorities. If improved manufacturing methods are promoted among the people in the future, the aforementioned difficulties can be resolved. Even if trade cannot increase immediately, it will eventually recover, prosper, and restore its former glory. Therefore, improving the green tea trade is not a major difficulty; it only requires merchants to sacrifice temporarily, resolutely ban coloring, and adopt new manufacturing methods.

As for black tea, foreign teas are manufactured indoors and fermented thoroughly, resulting in a bright and rich color that is pleasing to the eye. However, apart from the color, both the aroma and taste are far inferior to Chinese tea. If we can improve our manufacturing methods to make the tea more fermented and richer in color, in addition to its inherent aroma and taste, it will not be difficult to displace Ceylon and Indian teas and dominate the world market.

Therefore, improving manufacturing methods is crucial for developing China's tea trade. The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry recently dispatched specialists to guide the tea research stations in Hunan, Jiangxi, and Anhui provinces to adopt new manufacturing methods. The new tea produced this year has been inspected, and the color of various black teas is richer than those produced by the old methods. The color of various green teas is as green as jade and can be stored for a long time. This can be considered the first success in improving Chinese tea manufacturing methods, a truly gratifying event.

In addition to manufacturing methods, promotion is also important. China's foreign tea trade has long been monopolized by foreign firms, with very few direct promotions in foreign markets. Due to a lack of publicity, foreigners are often unaware of the quality of Chinese tea and are instead misled by the one-sided promotions of Indian and Japanese merchants. Therefore, after manufacturing methods are improved, improvements in international promotion and direct trade can secure the prosperity of China's tea trade. Recently, a Chinese consul stationed in England suggested that China should cultivate Indian tea varieties for improvement. However, the quality of Chinese tea is the best in the world, and Indian tea was originally transplanted from China. It's just that others know how to adapt and improve with the times, while we stick to old methods and lag behind.

People often cite high costs and heavy taxes as obstacles to developing commodity sales. However, if the quality is not improved and promotion is inadequate, even if the price is low, it will ultimately be rejected.
